# Changelog

All notable changes to TagPulse will be documented in this file.

## Unreleased

### Fixed

- **CI: complete the `build-and-push` GHCR attestation fix from PR #56 by also disabling buildx's embedded SLSA provenance attestation.** PR #56 swapped the attestation step's `subject-digest` from `steps.push.outputs.digest` (local image id) to `fromJSON(steps.push.outputs.metadata)['containerimage.digest']` (canonical buildx digest), but the post-merge `main`-branch run ([26066895103](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/actions/runs/26066895103)) still failed with the same `OCIError: 404` â€” just on a *different* digest. Root cause turned out to have a second layer the first PR missed: under `load: true` + `push: true`, buildx generates an **OCI image index** that wraps the image manifest + an embedded SLSA-provenance attestation manifest, but `load: true` forces single-manifest output to the docker daemon, so buildx pushes only the flat image manifest to the registry â€” never the index. `containerimage.digest` reports the **index** digest (`sha256:20f11062â€¦`), which is what we now feed to `actions/attest-build-provenance@v1` â€” but that digest isn't at GHCR, only `sha256:5319a655â€¦` (the flat image manifest that was actually pushed) is. Fix adds `provenance: false` to the `docker/build-push-action@v6` step, which tells buildx to skip the embedded provenance attestation and emit a flat single-platform manifest whose digest matches what's pushed. No supply-chain signal is lost â€” `actions/attest-build-provenance@v1` still generates SLSA provenance via GitHub's attestation API (the canonical source for this repo) and now successfully pushes the signed attestation as a referrer in GHCR. The inline comment in the workflow is updated to document both layers of the trap (`load: true` + `outputs.digest` bug AND the OCI-index-not-pushed bug) so the next person editing the workflow doesn't reintroduce either. Files: `.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml`.

- **CI: fix `build-and-push` workflow 404 in the GHCR provenance step on every push to `main`.** Symptom: each of the three image jobs (`api`, `worker`, `migrations`) succeeded at `docker/build-push-action@v6` (manifest pushed to both GHCR + the dev ACR) but then failed at `actions/attest-build-provenance@v1` with `OCIError: Error uploading artifact to container registry â€” Error fetching https://ghcr.io/v2/9owlsboston/tagpulse-<component>/manifests/sha256:<X> - expected 200, received 404`. Root cause: the attestation step's `subject-digest: ${{ steps.push.outputs.digest }}` was returning a **different** digest than what the build step actually pushed to GHCR â€” the build log showed e.g. `pushing manifest for ghcr.io/9owlsboston/tagpulse-worker:latest@sha256:ef4190cfâ€¦` while the attestation step requested `sha256:9be14d895câ€¦`. This is the known [docker/build-push-action#1015](https://github.com/docker/build-push-action/issues/1015) interaction between `load: true` (which the Sprint 26 D2 tools-image smoke needs to `docker run` the api image locally) and `push: true` â€” `outputs.digest` falls back to the **local image id** instead of the remote **manifest digest** when both are set. PR runs were unaffected because the attestation step is gated on `if: github.event_name != 'pull_request'`, which masked the bug behind successful PR CI ever since the workflow landed in Sprint 22 B3. Fix replaces `subject-digest: ${{ steps.push.outputs.digest }}` with `subject-digest: ${{ fromJSON(steps.push.outputs.metadata)['containerimage.digest'] }}` in [`.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml`](.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml), which reads the canonical manifest digest from buildx's `--metadata-file` JSON (the same value buildx prints in the `pushing manifest for â€¦ @sha256:â€¦` line) and is invariant under `load: true`. Inline comment documents the trap so the next person editing the workflow doesn't reintroduce it. **Note**: this fix turned out to be incomplete â€” see the follow-up entry above for the second layer (`provenance: false`) that was needed to close the 404. Files: `.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml`.

- **CORS: allow Azure Static Web App preview-slot URLs via `allow_origin_regex`.** Reported breakage: SPAs served from a SWA preview slot (per-PR hostnames like `https://<basename>-42.centralus.7.azurestaticapps.net`) failed every backend `fetch()` with a CORS preflight rejection because `cors_origins` is an exact-match comma list and preview hostnames cannot be enumerated ahead of time. Fix wires a new `CORS_ORIGIN_REGEX` env var end-to-end: [`Settings.cors_origin_regex`](src/tagpulse/core/config.py) (defaults to `""`, validated at boot with `re.compile` so a typo fails fast instead of surfacing as a 500 mid-request); [`api/main.py`](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) forwards it to Starlette `CORSMiddleware` as `allow_origin_regex` (empty string â†’ `None`, so the explicit allow-list path is unchanged when the regex is unset); [`/health/ready`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py) `_config_snapshot()` surfaces the value alongside `cors.allow_origins` so operators can verify the regex landed on the deployed revision without exec'ing into the container. **Bicep wiring**: [`modules/container-app.bicep`](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep) accepts a new optional `corsOriginRegex` param and emits the `CORS_ORIGIN_REGEX` env var beside the existing `CORS_ORIGINS` entry; [`workload.bicep`](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep) auto-derives a regex from `ui.outputs.defaultHostname` that matches the production hostname AND its preview slots (`^https://<basename>(-\d+)?(\.[a-z0-9-]+)?\.<tier>\.azurestaticapps\.net$`), with a new `corsOriginRegexOverride` param ([`main.bicepparam`](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam) reads it from the `CORS_ORIGIN_REGEX` env var) for the rare case an operator needs to tighten/broaden it. Worker container is unaffected (no ingress). **Tests** â€” [`tests/unit/test_cors_origin_regex.py`](tests/unit/test_cors_origin_regex.py) (new) covers: Settings default empty, invalid regex rejection, env-var wiring, `/health/ready` surface (set + unset), live `CORSMiddleware` preflight against three SWA hostname shapes (prod, preview no region, preview with region), rejection of three non-matching shapes (wrong basename / wrong suffix / wrong scheme), and Bicep wiring assertions for all five edits. `make check` clean. Files: `src/tagpulse/core/config.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py`, `deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep`, `deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep`, `deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam`, `tests/unit/test_cors_origin_regex.py`.

### Changed

- **Sprint 41 Phase H â€” close ADR 019 by dropping `assets.asset_type` (breaking API change) + Phase G5 ADR 019 docs close-out.** Completes the Categories cutover that started in Sprint 34 ADR 019 ("`asset_type` is dropped in a future migration once UI + clients have switched"). Sprint 41 Phase F7 brought the UI side (visible `Type` field gone from Asset create/edit forms); this Phase H ships the backend half on the same Sprint 41 PR rather than deferring it as the immediately-preceding Phase G CHANGELOG entry originally suggested. The deferral note in that entry is now historical â€” Phase H landed in the same PR. **Breaking** for any external API caller that still sends `?asset_type=` or reads `asset_type` off `Asset*` payloads. **H1 migration** [`migrations/versions/041_drop_assets_asset_type.py`](migrations/versions/041_drop_assets_asset_type.py): four-step `upgrade()` runs as the table owner without `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` per the established Sprint 38 migration 037 pattern â€” (a) JOIN-backfills `assets.category_id` from `categories.name` keyed off the legacy `asset_type` so existing rows pick up the structured FK that ADR 019 introduced as nullable; (b) safety-net seeds a per-tenant `_uncategorized` Category (`category_type='object'`, `required_tags=1`) and assigns any remaining NULL `category_id` rows to it â€” defends against rows that were created via the asset_type-only legacy path between ADR 019 and Phase H without an explicit category and ensures the subsequent NOT NULL promotion can't fail mid-migration; (c) `ALTER TABLE assets ALTER COLUMN category_id SET NOT NULL` makes the FK permanent; (d) `DROP INDEX IF EXISTS ix_assets_tenant_type` then `ALTER TABLE assets DROP COLUMN asset_type`. Every step is guarded by `information_schema` checks so a partial rerun (e.g. after a migration crash) is idempotent. Symmetric `downgrade()` re-adds the column nullable, backfills from `categories.name`, promotes to NOT NULL, and recreates `ix_assets_tenant_type` â€” round-trippable. **H2 schemas** [`src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py): removed `asset_type` from `AssetCreate` / `AssetUpdate` / `AssetResponse` / `ManifestEntry` / `ManifestResponse` / `AssetInZoneSummary`. `AssetCreate.category_id` is now **required** (was nullable during the ADR 019 compatibility window) and `AssetResponse.category_id` is now required non-Optional. `AssetUpdate.category_id` stays `UUID | None` with the "omit = no change" PATCH semantics; the API layer rejects an explicit `null` per the established Sprint 34 pattern. **H3 service + repos** â€” `AssetService.list_assets` ([`src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py`](src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py)) drops the `asset_type` parameter; `create_asset`'s audit-log `changes` dict now writes `{"name": ..., "category_id": str(asset.category_id)}` instead of the old `{"name", "asset_type", ...}` triple. `TimescaleAssetRepository` ([`src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/assets.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/assets.py)) drops the `AssetModel.asset_type` filter branch + the `_asset_to_response` mapping, including both arms of the `get_descendants` recursive CTE (anchor + recursive â€” neither references the dropped column anymore). `asset_location.py` ([`src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py)) drops the `a.asset_type` raw-SQL columns from `_ASSETS_IN_READER_BOUND_ZONE` and `_ASSETS_LATEST_GPS_READ`, and the `AssetInZoneSummary` list comprehensions that consumed them. **H4 route** [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/assets.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/assets.py): `GET /assets` drops the `asset_type: str | None = Query(...)` parameter and gets a one-release migration hint â€” any request that still carries an `?asset_type=` query param (including empty values) is rejected with **HTTP 400** before the label-filter parse, with detail `"The ?asset_type= query parameter was removed in Sprint 41 (ADR 019 close-out). Use ?category_id=<uuid> instead â€” list categories at GET /v1/tenants/{slug}/categories."`. The guard carries an inline `# Drop this guard in Sprint 42.` TODO so the next sprint can mechanically clear it; the hint is intentionally specific enough that a CI grep in a downstream consumer can map it to a concrete migration step. **H5 tests** â€” updated 8 unit/integration test files (plus 1 new regression file = 9 touched in total) to drop `asset_type` from fixtures and supply `category_id=uuid4()` where the schema now requires it: `tests/unit/test_asset_service.py` (factory + `_FakeAssetRepo` create signature + list signature + new audit assertion `audit.entries[-1]["changes"]["category_id"] == str(cid)`), `tests/unit/test_carrier_external.py` (factory + `_FakeAssetRepo.set_parent` clone + 3 test bodies dropping per-test `asset_type=` overrides), `tests/unit/test_categories.py` (7 `AssetCreate(...)` constructions switched from `asset_type="drum"` to `category_id=uuid4()`; renamed `test_category_id_optional_on_create` â†’ `test_category_id_required_on_create` to reflect the schema change), `tests/unit/test_asset_location.py` (factory + `AssetInZoneSummary` construction), `tests/unit/test_sprint21_caches.py` (factory; `uuid4` was already imported), `tests/unit/test_sprint19_subject_telemetry.py` (2 `AssetResponse` constructions), `tests/unit/test_label_filter.py` (`asset_type` â†’ `category_id` in the unrelated-params smoke test), `tests/unit/test_assets_repository_filters.py` (dropped the `asset_type="pallet"` kwarg + the `"assets.asset_type ="` SQL assert from the combines-with-other-filters test; status/category_id/ilike asserts retained). New file [`tests/unit/test_assets_route_asset_type_removed.py`](tests/unit/test_assets_route_asset_type_removed.py) covers the 400 guard with three FastAPI-TestClient tests using `app.dependency_overrides` for `get_current_user` (viewer role) and `get_asset_service` (stub returning `[]`): `test_asset_type_query_returns_400_with_migration_hint` (asserts `"asset_type"` + `"category_id"` + `"Sprint 41"` all appear in the detail), `test_asset_type_empty_value_still_returns_400` (defends against `?asset_type=` with an empty value sneaking past via FastAPI's empty-string coercion), and `test_list_assets_without_asset_type_still_works` (regression: the new guard doesn't false-positive on requests that don't carry the param). **H6 EPC parser stays** â€” [`src/tagpulse/rfid/epc.py`](src/tagpulse/rfid/epc.py)'s `asset_type_bits` / `asset_type` local variables and the `"asset_type"` dict key in its returned payload are GRAI URI bit-allocation semantics from the RFID protocol, not the dropped DB column; left untouched per the original roadmap plan. **Scripts** â€” [`scripts/simulate_assets.py`](scripts/simulate_assets.py) gains an `ensure_pallet_category(client, tenant_id)` helper that does a `GET /categories?limit=1000` lookup for the name "Sim-Pallet" and creates it on miss with `{"name": "Sim-Pallet", "category_type": "rti_container", "required_tags": 1}`; `ensure_assets()` calls it and uses `"category_id": category_id` in the POST payload instead of the dropped `"asset_type": "pallet"`. [`scripts/smoke_setup.py::ensure_assets_with_bindings`](scripts/smoke_setup.py) mirrors the same pattern inline at the top of the function. **G5 â€” ADR 019 close-out** ships in this same commit per the Phase G entry's original plan: [docs/adr/019-categories.md](docs/adr/019-categories.md) Status flipped to `**Completed** (Sprint 41 close-out, [PR #54](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/54) â€” accepted Sprint 34, May 2026; compatibility window closed Sprint 41, Phase H)` with the migration paragraph rewritten in past tense citing migrations 037 + 041; [docs/data-models.md](docs/data-models.md) drops the `assets.asset_type` table row, flips `assets.category_id` to NOT NULL with a note about Sprint 41 Phase H migration 041, and updates the Migration provenance line to `"017 (base table); 037 adds category_id; 041 promotes category_id to NOT NULL and drops asset_type"`; [docs/design/assets-and-zones.md](docs/design/assets-and-zones.md) CREATE TABLE swaps `asset_type VARCHAR(50)` for `category_id UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES categories(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT`, the index renames `ix_assets_tenant_category`, the paragraph is rewritten to reference ADR-019 + Sprint 41 Phase H, the no-quantity callout's `GROUP BY` and the `AssetRepository.list` signature are updated to `category_id`; [docs/design/tracking-modes.md](docs/design/tracking-modes.md) example query changes to `WHERE category_id = '<forklift-category>'`; [docs/design/geofencing-and-map.md](docs/design/geofencing-and-map.md) two `asset_filter` blocks change `asset_type: pallet`/`container` to `category_id: <pallet-category-uuid>`/`<container-category-uuid>`; [docs/guides/domain-concepts-101.md](docs/guides/domain-concepts-101.md) curl example uses `"name": "Sim-Pallet-03", "category_id": "<pallet-category-uuid>"`. **Roadmap reconciliation** â€” [docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md) Phase H section drops its "(deferred to a follow-up sprint)" header + the standalone deferral status blockquote, flips H1â€“H6 from `[planned]` to `[done, this PR]` with implementation notes inline, F7's "(still carrying the column until Phase H)" / "Phase H ... is deferred" language reworded to past tense, and G5 flipped from `[deferred to a follow-up sprint]` to `[done, this PR]`. [ADR 021](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) v2.2 decision-history block rewritten â€” the "Phase H deferred" paragraph is replaced with "Phase H shipped in the same Sprint 41 PR as the original plan" + a recap of the migration strategy + the breaking-change scope + the one-release HTTP 400 hint. **openapi.json regenerated** via `python scripts/export_openapi.py` â€” `AssetCreate.category_id` is now `required`; `AssetResponse.category_id` is now `required` non-nullable; `AssetUpdate.category_id` stays optional; `ManifestEntry.asset_type` / `ManifestResponse.asset_type` / `AssetInZoneSummary.asset_type` / `AssetCreate.asset_type` / `AssetUpdate.asset_type` / `AssetResponse.asset_type` all removed; the `asset_type` query parameter on `GET /assets` removed. **`make check` clean.** Migration / API / SDK consumers need a one-line change: stop sending `?asset_type=`, send `?category_id=<uuid>` instead (categories listable at `GET /v1/tenants/{slug}/categories`). `migrations/versions/041_drop_assets_asset_type.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/assets.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/assets.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py`, `scripts/simulate_assets.py`, `scripts/smoke_setup.py`, `tests/unit/test_asset_service.py`, `tests/unit/test_carrier_external.py`, `tests/unit/test_categories.py`, `tests/unit/test_asset_location.py`, `tests/unit/test_sprint21_caches.py`, `tests/unit/test_sprint19_subject_telemetry.py`, `tests/unit/test_label_filter.py`, `tests/unit/test_assets_repository_filters.py`, `tests/unit/test_assets_route_asset_type_removed.py`, `docs/adr/019-categories.md`, `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`, `docs/data-models.md`, `docs/design/assets-and-zones.md`, `docs/design/tracking-modes.md`, `docs/design/geofencing-and-map.md`, `docs/guides/domain-concepts-101.md`, `docs/roadmap.md`, `openapi.json`.

### Added

- **Sprint 41 Phase G â€” documentation reconciliation for Configurable Signaling Events (ADR 021 v2 ratification + remediation row flips + user-guide section).** Closes the docs half of Sprint 41 after backend Phases Aâ€“E (PR [#54](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/54), `e54332b` â†’ `975ef6f`) and UI Phase F (TagPulse-UI [PR #46](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI/pull/46), `ebb2f82`) shipped. **G1 â€” ADR 021 ratified Proposed â†’ Accepted** in [`docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md): Status header flipped to "Accepted (Sprint 41, May 2026)" with back-links to PR #54 (backend) and TagPulse-UI PR #46 (UI); v2.2 entry appended to the Â§"Decision history" recording the per-phase commit chain, the four v2.1 open-question leans resolving as leaned (kind="signaling" stays `VARCHAR + pattern` not Postgres ENUM; discriminator is the in-process two-level `split_signaling_condition_type` helper not Pydantic `Field(discriminator=...)`; per-rule `integration_ids` **replace** the global broadcast when non-empty per Phase E2 pinned by `test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py::TestPerRuleReplace`; default cap of 5 per `(event_type, category_id)` is hard-reject with admin-only `?override=true` writing one `audit_logs` row per Phase B2 pinned by `test_signaling_rules_api.py`); ADR Â§"Open questions" rewritten to mark all Sprint 41 questions resolved and forward-point only the cross-ADR items (ADR 024 trilateration Sprint 45, post-Sprint-41 rule taxonomy unification). The "signaling" terminology is now load-bearing across schema columns (`event_type`, `trigger`, `processor`), service classes (`SignalingScopeCapExceededError`, `validate_signaling_condition_config`), modules (`src/tagpulse/signaling/`), event-bus topics (`signaling.attribution_settled`), API discriminator (`?kind=signaling`), and UI components (`SignalingRuleModal`, `SignalingEventType`, `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS`) â€” a future revert to "sensing" would be a multi-PR sweep, so v2.2 explicitly notes the taxonomy choice is locked. **G2 â€” Four reference-design remediation rows flipped to âœ… Done** in [`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) per the doc's own Â§7 "Updating this document" rule: Â§3.1 row 2.3 (Configurable Signaling Events backend) â†’ âœ… Done with PR #54 commit range `e54332b â†’ 975ef6f` covering Phases Aâ€“E; row 2.9 (Outbound event envelope) â†’ âœ… Done with `feae604` (Phase C) and a per-event-type identity-key recap (`location` â†’ `[asset_id, zone_id]`, `geolocation` â†’ `[asset_id, site_id]`, `geofencing` â†’ `[asset_id, zone_id]`, `temperature` â†’ `[asset_id]`); Â§3.2 row 1.1 ("Unify Telemetry/Models/Rules/Alerts â†’ Signaling Events & Data") â†’ âœ… Done with TagPulse-UI PR #46 `ebb2f82` â€” column relabeled "Signaling Events & Data" (the v2.1 sensingâ†’signaling rename is consistent across the surface so the sidebar group label matches schema + event-bus + React component naming); row 3.5 ("Signaling Events modal") â†’ âœ… Done with the same UI commit and a callout that the 13-pair `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS` matrix rejects impossible pairs (`temperature.on_entry`, `geofencing.on_change`) client-side before submit. **G3 â€” User-guide section "Configurable Signaling Events"** added to [`docs/user-guide.md`](docs/user-guide.md) between the existing Rules and Alerts sections (TOC + anchor + ~150 lines): "What's new vs. legacy rules" comparison table; the authoritative 13-pair event-type Ã— trigger matrix with a one-line rationale per restriction (`on_inference` is `location`-only because OverlappingZones is the only processor that publishes `signaling.attribution_settled`; `geofencing` triggers are spatial primitives that don't apply to subject-bound metric streams); a four-step "Creating a Signaling Event" walkthrough that maps to the Phase F2 modal screens; **four curl recipes** â€” Location `on_change` (high-value asset zone change with `cooldown_s=300`, scoped to one Category); Temperature `periodic` (daily cold-chain digest with `cadence_minutes=1440`, scoped to one Category); Geofencing `on_entry` (restricted-zone breach with explicit `zone_id` + `subject_kinds=["asset"]` + `cooldown_s=60`, broadcast scope); Geolocation `on_inactivity` (GPS asset silent > 60 min with `inactivity_minutes=60` + `cooldown_s=300`, scoped to one Category) â€” all POST to the unified `/v1/tenants/{slug}/rules` endpoint with `"kind": "signaling"` body (no `/sensing-events` URL, per Phase E1 deviation); plus sections on listing (`?kind=signaling` filter), the per-scope cap + admin override semantics (HTTP 409 / `?override=true` + audit-log row), and the per-rule webhook routing replace-not-augment behaviour pinned by `test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py::TestPerRuleReplace`. **Roadmap reconciliation** â€” every [planned] marker on Sprint 41 Phases A through G in [`docs/roadmap.md`](docs/roadmap.md) flipped to [done] with the implementing commit SHA inline; Phase E1 explicitly attributed to Phase B2 commit `9f02f38` (the discriminator filter shipped on the existing `/rules` endpoint at Phase B time, not Phase E time â€” the per-roadmap deviation from the original `/sensing-events` URL proposal); Phase A4 attributed to both `e54332b` (helper + lookup table) and `9f02f38` (per-trigger config models) since the Pydantic foundation landed across the Aâ†’B handoff. **Phase H + G5 update (post-commit):** the original Phase G commit landed with Phase H deferred to a follow-up sprint with its plan preserved verbatim in roadmap Â§"Phase H"; the deferral was **revoked later in the same Sprint 41 PR** â€” Phase H + G5 shipped together (see the Phase H entry above this one). At Phase G commit time the Phase F7 UI work already dropped the **visible** `Type` field on Asset forms (a hidden `Form.Item` pinned `asset_type` so the backend, still carrying the column, kept round-tripping cleanly). Pure documentation â€” no source, no tests, no migration, no behaviour change in this Phase G slice itself. `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`, `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`, `docs/user-guide.md`, `docs/roadmap.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase F â€” UI surface for Configurable Signaling Events (ADR-021 v2) shipped on TagPulse-UI [PR #46](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI/pull/46) (`ebb2f82`).** Backend cross-link entry â€” the UI work ships in a separate repo per the long-standing TagPulse / TagPulse-UI split, but is sprint-tied to this backend PR via [ADR 021 v2.2](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) and the reference-design remediation rows 1.1 + 3.5 (both flipped âœ… Done in the Phase G commit above). Files-changed: 20 (+1,726 / âˆ’100), 3 new. `npm run check` clean (lint + typecheck + 208/208 vitest). **F1 â€” Signaling Events sidebar group** in `src/components/Layout.tsx` consolidates Rules + Alerts under one Ant Menu `type: 'group'` header per UI gap 1.1; final label is "Signaling Events" (the v2.1 sensingâ†’signaling rename is consistent across the rest of the surface). **F2 â€” `SignalingRuleModal`** at `src/pages/rules/SignalingRuleModal.tsx` walks Event Type â†’ Trigger (validated against the 13-pair `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS` matrix in `src/types.ts` â€” impossible pairs hidden from the dropdown, not greyed) â†’ per-trigger config form â†’ optional Category / Label / Integration scoping; form POSTs to `/v1/tenants/{slug}/rules` with `"kind": "signaling"` body (no `/sensing-events` URL, per backend Phase E1). **F3 â€” RuleEditor Tabs wrapper** at `src/pages/rules/RuleEditor.tsx` makes "Signaling Event" the default create tab with a "Legacy rule" sub-tab keeping the 10 legacy `condition_type` form editable for round-tripping. **F4 â€” vitest coverage** in `SignalingRuleModal.test.tsx` (NEW, 16 cases) parametrizes all 13 valid pairs + 4 invalid-pair rejections; uses `PointerEventsCheckLevel.Never` + 15s per-test timeout + explicit `afterEach(cleanup)` to handle AntD motion + Select interactions cleanly. **F5 â€” Sidebar reorganization** consolidates top-level groups: DATA MANAGEMENT (Assets, Categories, Sites, Labels) / EDGE MANAGEMENT (Devices, Integrations) / SIGNALING EVENTS (Rules, Alerts) / INVENTORY. **F6 â€” Collapsible icon-mode sidebar** â€” Ant `Sider` with `collapsible` + `collapsedWidth={64}`; tooltips when collapsed; preference persisted in `localStorage` keyed `(tenantId, userId)` so each operator's setting travels with their account. **Surfaced + fixed a real bug** while writing F8 tests: `Sider.onCollapse(_, 'responsive')` fires on jsdom mount (default `matchMedia` returns `matches: false`) and was clobbering the persisted preference; the fix in `handleSiderCollapse(next, type)` only writes to `localStorage` when `type === 'clickTrigger'`. **F7 â€” Asset form drops visible `Type` field** in `src/pages/assets/AssetList.tsx` + `src/pages/assets/AssetDetail.tsx`; a hidden `Form.Item` pins `asset_type` to `'asset'` for create and preserves existing values for edit so the backend (still carrying the column until Phase H) keeps round-tripping cleanly. **F8 â€” `Layout.test.tsx`** (NEW, 4 cases) covers the collapsed-sidebar toggle + persistence shape + the responsive-event regression guard from F6. The regenerated OpenAPI client (`src/api/generated/*` after `npm run generate-api`) picks up Phase E's `RuleCreate` / `RuleUpdate` / `RuleResponse` signaling fields + the `kind` discriminator + the `?kind=` query param. No backend source change in this entry â€” purely a sprint-tied cross-link so a search of this repo's CHANGELOG for "Sprint 41" surfaces all eight phases.

- **Sprint 41 Phase E â€” API surface for Configurable Signaling Events (ADR-021 v2): per-rule integration routing + OpenAPI regen.** Closes the API-layer half of Sprint 41 after Phases Aâ€“D (schema â†’ service/dispatcher shell â†’ outbound envelope â†’ processors + on_inference). **E1 â€” `?kind=signaling` discriminator filter** was already shipped in Phase B2 on the existing `/v1/tenants/{slug}/rules` endpoint (per the roadmap deviation from ADR-021's original `/sensing-events` URL proposal â€” avoids baking a legacy URL into the API at the moment the deferred Sprint-4X taxonomy-unification ADR plans to rename `rules` â†’ `alert_rules` anyway); this entry pins that decision and confirms no parallel URL namespace was added in Phase E. **E2 â€” per-rule integration routing** in [`src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`](src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py). Implements [ADR-021 v2 open question #3](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) â€” *replace, not augment*: when a rule's `integration_ids` column is non-empty, the WebhookDispatcher delivers the resulting alert **only** to integrations in that allow-list (intersected with the subscription set for the event type); when the column is empty or null, the dispatcher falls back to the legacy broadcast over every enabled integration subscribed to the event. Renames the internal helper `_build_alert_envelope` â†’ `_resolve_alert_rule_context` so a single `session.get(RuleModel, rule_uuid)` per dispatcher tick now feeds **both** the Phase-C envelope build **and** the Phase-E integration filter â€” no second DB lookup. Helper returns `tuple[dict[str, Any], frozenset[uuid.UUID] | None]` where the second element is `None` for "broadcast" and a `frozenset` for "filter to these integration IDs". Gated on `event.topic == Topic.ALERT_TRIGGERED` so non-alert broadcasts (raw `tag_read.created`, `telemetry.recorded`) are never filtered â€” they have no rule context to consult. Three defensive paths preserve the legacy broadcast behaviour: missing `rule_id` in payload â†’ broadcast; malformed `rule_id` (not a UUID) â†’ broadcast; unknown `rule_id` (rule deleted between publish and dispatch) â†’ broadcast (rather than silently dropping the alert when the operator's intent has been lost). Two intentional non-defensive paths: rule with non-empty `integration_ids` that don't intersect the subscription set â†’ **zero deliveries** (the rule's allow-list mis-config is surfaced as missing webhook calls, not papered over with a fallback broadcast); rule allow-listing a not-subscribed integration â†’ that integration is skipped (the filter intersects with the subscription set, doesn't bypass it). **E2 tests** â€” new [`tests/unit/test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py`](tests/unit/test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py) (12 tests, four `Test*` classes) mirrors the Phase C `test_webhook_envelope.py` scaffolding (same `_FakeMeter`, same `httpx.MockTransport`-backed handler that captures the request URL so the test asserts which integrations were hit, same `IntegrationService` patch that returns a controlled subscription list). `TestBroadcastFallback` (2 tests) â€” null and empty `integration_ids` both broadcast to every enabled subscribed integration. `TestPerRuleReplace` (3 tests) â€” subset allow-list delivers only to the subset; allow-list with a not-subscribed integration ID skips it (replace âˆ© subscribe, not bypass); allow-list disjoint from subscription set delivers nothing. `TestPerRuleReplaceSignaling` (4 tests, parametrized over the 4 event types) â€” signaling rules (event_type populated) honour the filter the same way as legacy rules; the filter is event-type-agnostic by design. `TestFilterDefensivePaths` (3 tests) â€” missing `rule_id` / unknown `rule_id` / non-alert event all fall through to broadcast. **E3 â€” OpenAPI regen** via `python scripts/export_openapi.py > openapi.json`. The regenerated spec picks up the Phase A schema additions on `RuleCreate` / `RuleUpdate` / `RuleResponse` (`event_type` enum, `trigger`, `processor`, `confidence_threshold` `NUMERIC(3,2)` constrained to `[0.0, 1.0]`, `category_ids` UUID array, `asset_label_filters` / `zone_label_filters` / `site_label_filters` JSONB arrays, `integration_ids` UUID array), the extended `condition_type` regex covering the 12 `signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>` pairs alongside the 10 legacy values, the `kind: Literal["legacy", "signaling"]` discriminator on `RuleResponse`, and the `?kind=` query param on `GET /rules`. Diff stat: `+413/-2` lines in `openapi.json` (374,625 â†’ 386,342 bytes). The outbound webhook envelope fields (`confidence`, `keySet`, `eventConfigurationId`, `categoryId`, `labels`) are intentionally **not** in the OpenAPI spec â€” they're outbound payload fields on the webhook delivery itself, not API request/response schema, so they live in the ADR-021 v2 Â§"Outbound envelope" section and the dispatcher tests (`test_webhook_envelope.py` Phase C; `test_signaling_envelope.py` builder). **`make check` clean: 1073 unit tests passing** (was 1061 before Phase E; +12 from the new per-rule-routing test file), `ruff check src tests` âœ“, `mypy --strict` âœ“. Phase E completes the API-surface half of Sprint 41 â€” only Phases F (UI), G (docs reconciliation), and H (drop `assets.asset_type`) remain. `src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`, `tests/unit/test_webhook_per_rule_routing.py`, `openapi.json`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase D â€” IsolatedZones + OverlappingZones processors + `on_inference` alert consumer (ADR-021 v2).** Lands the real Phase D processor pipeline that Phases Aâ€“C set up, completing the rule-evaluation half of Sprint 41. **D1 IsolatedZones module** [`src/tagpulse/signaling/isolated_zones.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/isolated_zones.py): pure-function codification of the existing "one read â†’ at most one zone" attribution rule used by the ingestion path. Public surface: `ZoneCandidate` dataclass (id, kind, created_at, fixed_reader_ids, polygon_geojson, bbox_min/max_lat/lon); `IsolatedZoneAttribution` (zone_id, zone_kind, sourceâˆˆ{"reader_bound","geofence"}); `attribute_reader_bound(read_reader_id, zones)` and `attribute_geofence(latitude, longitude, zones)` that match independently; `attribute(reader_id, latitude, longitude, zones)` chains the two with reader-bound priority + geofence fallback. Deterministic-oldest tiebreak (`min(..., key=lambda z: z.created_at)`) matches `TimescaleSitesZonesRepository.get_zone_for_reader` and `IngestionService._eval_geofence_for_subject`. Geofence path uses the `bbox_*` denormalized columns as a cheap O(1) prefilter before the ring ray-cast via `tagpulse.geo.point_in_polygon` (which expects ring coords as `(lon, lat)` tuples â€” see [`src/tagpulse/geo/__init__.py`](src/tagpulse/geo/__init__.py)); malformed `polygon_geojson` payloads are silently skipped so one bad zone can't poison the loop for the rest of the tenant. No DB I/O â€” the module is callable from any code path that has already loaded the zone candidates. Phase D1 doesn't change ingestion behaviour â€” it extracts the existing logic into a reusable shape so the upcoming `IsolatedZonesProcessor` (future periodic runner that mirrors the ingestion attribution for retrospective queries) can share the same pure functions. **D2 OverlappingZones module** [`src/tagpulse/signaling/overlapping_zones.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/overlapping_zones.py): two layers. *Pure layer* â€” `AttributionRead` (asset_id, reader_id, timestamp, signal_strength, latitude, longitude); `AggregationConfig` (aggregation_window_s=60, min_rssi_dbm=-80.0, zone_bleed_filter=True, zone_bleed_share_threshold=0.10, aging_weight=1.0, aging_bucket_s=60, time_error_filter_s=5) with `from_rule_config(condition_config)` classmethod that uses **tri-state** logic for `min_rssi_dbm` â€” missing key â†’ default `-80.0`, explicit `null` â†’ `None` (floor disabled), numeric â†’ coerce to float (regression-pinned in `test_aggregation_config_from_rule_config_*`); `ZoneAttribution` (asset_id, zone_id, site_id, confidence, window_start, window_end, contributing_reads, contributing_readers); `_attributable_zones_for_read` returns **all** matching zones (unlike IsolatedZones which picks one) â€” multi-membership is the entire point of the overlapping processor; `_age_weight(read_age_s, window_s, weight, bucket_s)` decays older reads inside the window; `aggregate(reads, zones, *, now, site_by_zone, config)` is the workhorse â€” buckets evidence per `(asset, zone)` pair, normalizes confidences per asset, applies the bleed filter (drop zones whose share is strictly below `zone_bleed_share_threshold` with re-normalization of survivors), and returns a deterministically-ordered list sorted by `(str(asset_id), str(zone_id))` so two runs over the same input always emit attribution events in the same order. *Runtime layer* â€” `OverlappingZonesProcessor(event_bus)` with `async run_once_for_rule(session, rule, *, now=None) -> int`: loads zone candidates via SQLAlchemy `select(ZoneModel)`; loads in-window reads via raw `text()` SQL that joins `tag_reads Ã— asset_tag_bindings` on the three-way `binding_kind âˆˆ {epc, tid, device}` match (mirrors the existing `_PATH_SQL` join pattern in `tagpulse.repositories.timescaledb.asset_location`); calls `aggregate()`; publishes one `Topic.SIGNALING_ATTRIBUTION_SETTLED` event per attribution with the **coordinate-system-agnostic payload** pinned by [ADR-021 v2](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) Â§"`signaling.attribution_settled` payload": `{tenant_id, asset_id, zone_id, site_id, confidence, window_start, window_end, contributing_reads, contributing_readers, rule_id}` â€” explicitly **no** `latitude` / `longitude` / `x` / `y` / `position_*` fields (that's [ADR-024](docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md) territory, Sprint 45). The reads-query is parameterised by tenant_id and the configured window with skew tolerance (`window_start = now - aggregation_window_s - time_error_filter_s`); reads whose tag is unbound at the window time are silently excluded â€” they have no asset to attribute to. **Dispatcher dispatch-by-processor** in [`src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py): `PeriodicSignalingDispatcher.__init__` constructs `self._overlapping_processor = OverlappingZonesProcessor(event_bus)`; `_evaluate_periodic_rule` now dispatches by `rule.processor or "isolated_zones"` â€” `overlapping_zones` invokes `run_once_for_rule` inside a try/except so a single bad rule doesn't break the tick (pinned by `test_dispatch_overlapping_processor_error_does_not_break_tick`); `isolated_zones` (and None) stay at the Phase B logging shell since the IsolatedZones case is already covered by the ingestion path. The `rule_evaluations` meter tick fires once per rule regardless of processor so per-tenant counts remain comparable across operator choices. **`RuleEvaluator.on_attribution_settled`** in [`src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py`](src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py): new async consumer subscribed to `Topic.SIGNALING_ATTRIBUTION_SETTLED` (wired in [`src/tagpulse/api/main.py`](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) right after the existing `Topic.TELEMETRY_RECORDED` subscription in the `workers_inline=True` block). Iterates the three `signaling.<event_type>.on_inference` condition_types (`location` / `geolocation` / `temperature` â€” listed all three so a future temperature processor fans out the same way without re-touching this method); applies `min_confidence` from `condition_config` (default 0.0); applies cooldown keyed `(tenant_id, rule_id, asset_id_str)` matching the convention from `on_subject_zone_changed`; resolves asset name via `_lookup_subject_name(subject_kind="asset", ...)` and zone name via `_lookup_zone_name` so alert messages are human-readable; creates alert with `severity="info"` and publishes `Topic.ALERT_TRIGGERED` with the full `action_type`/`action_config` payload so the WebhookDispatcher path picks it up without a second DB lookup; ticks `rule_evaluations` per rule + `alerts_fired` per fired alert. Defensive paths: missing/invalid `tenant_id` â†’ silent return; missing `asset_id` / `zone_id` â†’ silent return; unparseable `confidence` â†’ silent return (these are pinned by the new test file). **Tests** â€” three new test files + 3 new tests added to the existing dispatcher file, 50 new tests total. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_isolated_zones.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_isolated_zones.py) (17 tests): reader-bound match/no-match/ignores-geofence/oldest-tiebreak/empty-fixed-list, geofence inside-polygon/outside-bbox/in-bbox-outside-L-shape/ignores-reader-bound/malformed-polygon-skipped/oldest-tiebreak, combined `attribute()` reader-priority/geofence-fallback/no-match/no-geofence-signal/no-reader-id/empty-list. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones.py) (27 tests): AggregationConfig defaults/full-from_rule_config/missing-block-defaults/explicit-null-rssi-disabled; aggregate empty cases; single-zone full confidence; multi-asset independence; genuine 50/50 overlap (reader-bound + geofence on same read); uneven 80/20 share; RSSI floor drop/None-passes/disabled-when-None; window enforcement (drops old, time_error_filter extends, drops future-beyond-skew); aging-weight 1-bucket-decay confidence_unchanged_single_zone, aging-shifts-overlap (1.0/1.5 vs 0.5/1.5); bleed filter at 19/1 â†’ drops B (10% threshold demands strictly-below, so 9/1=10% survives); bleed disabled keeps 0.95/0.05; deterministic output order; site_by_zone propagation; missing-site-dropped; three D3 synthetic-stream scenarios. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones_processor.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones_processor.py) (7 tests): DB-mocked `_FakeSession` routing the two `execute()` calls to canned zone + read results; zero-zones returns 0 (reads query is skipped); zero-reads returns 0; happy path emits one event per attribution with correct payload shape (asserts every payload key including `contributing_readers` list and `rule_id`); explicit **forbidden-coordinate-fields** check â€” asserts the emitted payload has no `latitude` / `longitude` / `lat` / `lon` / `x` / `y` keys even when the underlying `tag_reads` row carried them (defends ADR-021 v2's coordinate-system-agnostic pin against accidental field leakage in a future refactor); genuine overlap emits two events with `confidence=[0.5, 0.5]`; configured window is honoured (third read at 60s ago drops when window is 30s); reads-query parameters include `tenant_id` and the skew-extended window bounds. New dispatcher tests in [`tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py) (+3 tests, now 12): rule with `processor='overlapping_zones'` is routed to `OverlappingZonesProcessor.run_once_for_rule`, rule with `processor=None` is not; both processor variants record a `rule_evaluations` meter tick; a `RuntimeError` from the processor doesn't break the tick (`last_fired` still stamped for the good rule). [`tests/unit/test_signaling_on_inference.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_on_inference.py) (10 tests): happy path fires alert + meter ticks; below-threshold skips alert but still records `rule_evaluations`; cooldown suppresses the second event for the same asset; cooldown is keyed per `(tenant, rule, asset)` so a different asset triggers an independent alert; one attribution event fans out to all three `event_type` on_inference rules (location + geolocation + temperature); defensive paths: missing tenant_id, invalid tenant UUID, missing asset_id/zone_id, unparseable confidence; ALERT_TRIGGERED payload includes the rule's `action_type` + `action_config` so webhook delivery works without a second DB lookup. **`make check` clean: 1061 unit tests passing** (was 1011 before Phase D; +50 new), `ruff check src tests` âœ“, `mypy --strict` âœ“. Phase D leaves Phase E (API surface for the new `processor` enum + per-event-type rule constructors) and Phase F (UI) as the remaining Sprint 41 work. `src/tagpulse/signaling/isolated_zones.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/overlapping_zones.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`, `src/tagpulse/rules/evaluator.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_isolated_zones.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_overlapping_zones_processor.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_on_inference.py`.

- **Sprint 41 â€” pre-Phase-D coordinate-system clarification (docs only).** Pins the lat/lon-vs-local-`(x, y)` boundary in three docs so the OverlappingZones processor (Phase D) doesn't get conflated with true indoor trilateration ([ADR 024](docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md), Sprint 45). Surfaced by a customer-scenario question on PR #54 about warehouses that work in a local XY grid rather than WGS84. **No code change** â€” the audit confirmed the existing `zones.fixed_reader_ids` + `zones.polygon_geojson` model already covers both the indoor warehouse use case (reader-bound zones, no coordinates needed) and the outdoor lat/lon use case, and the Phase D processors are zone-membership processors that operate on `(asset, zone)` pairs rather than raw coordinates. Concretely: (1) [`docs/roadmap.md`](docs/roadmap.md) â€” Sprint 41 Phase D header gains a **"Coordinate-system scope"** blockquote spelling out that both processors emit `(asset, zone, confidence)` not `(x, y)`, that the membership primitives are `tag_reads.reader_id âˆˆ zones.fixed_reader_ids` (reader-bound) OR `(tag_reads.latitude, tag_reads.longitude) WITHIN zones.polygon_geojson` (WGS84 geofence), and that true `(x, y)` trilateration is a Sprint 45 / ADR-024 deliverable; (2) [`docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`](docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md) Â§"Processor implementation" gains a new **"`signaling.attribution_settled` payload â€” coordinate-system-agnostic"** sub-section pinning the event-bus payload shape: `{tenant_id, asset_id, zone_id, site_id, confidence, window_start, window_end, contributing_reads, contributing_readers, rule_id}` â€” explicitly no `latitude`/`longitude`/`x`/`y`/`position_*` fields, with a forward pointer to ADR 024 for `asset_positions` per-asset position fixes; (3) [`docs/user-guide.md`](docs/user-guide.md) Â§"Zones â€” three kinds" gains a **"What about local `(x, y)` coordinates inside a warehouse?"** callout immediately after the three-kinds table, telling warehouse operators to model aisles as `reader_bound` zones today and pointing at ADR 024 for the sub-meter trilateration story. Together these three edits give Phase D a coordinate-system-explicit handoff so the implementation PR doesn't drift into half-baked XY-in-`polygon_geojson` hacks, and give customers a single answer to the "we use x/y not lat/lon" question. `docs/roadmap.md`, `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`, `docs/user-guide.md`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase C â€” outbound webhook envelope upgrade (ADR-021 v2, closes remediation gap 2.9).** Adds five additive top-level fields to every rule-fired webhook payload (`confidence`, `keySet`, `eventConfigurationId`, `categoryId`, `labels`) so downstream consumers can reason about a fired event without a round-trip back to TagPulse to fetch the source rule or matched entity. Fires for **all rules** (legacy + signaling) â€” legacy rules get safe defaults (`confidence=1.0`, `keySet=[]`, `eventConfigurationId=str(rule_id)`, `categoryId=null`, `labels=[]`) so the change is fully additive: existing webhook consumers see every historical payload field unchanged and pick up five new keys they can ignore. Signaling rules populate `confidence` from `rules.confidence_threshold`, `keySet` from the per-event-type identity-key table (`location` â†’ `["asset_id", "zone_id"]`, `geolocation` â†’ `["asset_id", "site_id"]`, `geofencing` â†’ `["asset_id", "zone_id"]`, `temperature` â†’ `["asset_id"]`), and `eventConfigurationId` from `rules.id` â€” matches the worked example in [`docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md`](docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md) Â§"dispatcher-layer envelope". **C1 builder module** [`src/tagpulse/integrations/signaling_envelope.py`](src/tagpulse/integrations/signaling_envelope.py): pure (no I/O) `build_envelope(*, rule_id, event_type, confidence_threshold, category_id=None, labels=None) -> SignalingEnvelopeFields` + `derive_key_set(event_type) -> list[str]` + `_KEY_SETS` constant. Returns a `TypedDict` so callers spread it with `**envelope_fields` into the outer payload. Legacy branch pins `confidence=1.0` regardless of the threshold column value (the concept doesn't apply to legacy rules â€” the column is additive on every row); signaling branch coerces `Decimal` â†’ `float` (`NUMERIC(3,2)` from PG arrives as `Decimal` in SQLAlchemy 2.0). Defensive: missing `rule_id` â†’ `eventConfigurationId=None`; missing `confidence_threshold` on a signaling row â†’ 0.0 ("all"); unknown `event_type` â†’ empty `keySet`; `derive_key_set` returns a fresh list so callers can't corrupt the module-level table; `build_envelope` deep-copies `labels` so consumers can mutate without affecting cached matched-entity rows. **C2 dispatcher wiring** [`src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`](src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py): new `WebhookDispatcher._build_alert_envelope(session, payload) -> dict[str, Any]` helper looks up the source `RuleModel` once per tick (gated on `event.topic == Topic.ALERT_TRIGGERED` so raw broadcast events like `tag_read.created` and `telemetry.recorded` keep the pre-Phase-C envelope shape unchanged), calls `build_envelope` with the rule columns, and returns the five-field dict. `on_event` spreads `**envelope_fields` into the outer payload **once per tick** (not per integration â€” multiple subscribed webhooks share one DB lookup), positioned above `enrichments` so the existing "enrichments wins on key collision" precedent is preserved. Three defensive branches: missing `rule_id` â†’ empty dict (no new fields, falls back to pre-Phase-C shape); malformed `rule_id` (not a UUID) â†’ empty dict; unknown `rule_id` (deleted between publish and dispatch) â†’ safe defaults populated from the rule_id in the payload. `categoryId`/`labels` stay at safe defaults for both legacy and signaling paths in Phase C â€” Phase D will wire the matched-entity lookup once OverlappingZones publishes the subject identity on its alert payload. **C3 conformance tests** â€” two new test files, 34 new tests total. [`tests/unit/test_signaling_envelope.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_envelope.py) (24 tests, four `Test*` classes): `derive_key_set` for each of the 4 event_types + None + unknown + a fresh-copy regression guard; `build_envelope` legacy path (safe defaults; threshold column ignored; categoryId/labels passthrough when provided â€” Phase D forward-compat); signaling path (per-event_type keySet, `Decimal` and `float` threshold coercion, None threshold â†’ 0.0 fallback, eventConfigurationId from rule_id, categoryId UUID/string normalization, labels propagation, empty-labels â†’ empty-list, labels fresh-copy); defensive path (rule_id=None â†’ eventConfigurationId=None, UUID serialization). [`tests/unit/test_webhook_envelope.py`](tests/unit/test_webhook_envelope.py) (10 tests, four `Test*` classes) exercises the full dispatcher path against an `httpx.MockTransport`-backed client so assertions run against the actual on-the-wire JSON body a consumer would receive, not just the in-memory dict: (a) legacy rule preserves every historical alert field + gains the 5 new fields with safe defaults; (b) signaling rule populates `confidence`/`keySet`/`eventConfigurationId` per event_type (parametrized over all 4); (c) non-`ALERT_TRIGGERED` events (`Topic.TAG_READ_CREATED`) emit pre-Phase-C envelope with no new fields injected (regression guard against accidental fan-out); defensive paths cover missing `rule_id`, unknown `rule_id` (deleted rule), and malformed `rule_id`. Test infrastructure: `_build_dispatcher_with_fake_session` wires a fully-mocked async session whose `session.get` dispatches on `model is RuleModel` / `model is IntegrationModel` so a single fake covers both the envelope-builder lookup and the post-deliver `last_triggered` update; `IntegrationService` is patched in the `webhook` module to a stub that returns a controlled integration list without touching the DB. **No behaviour change for existing rules' historical fields** â€” the new fields are additive top-level keys; webhook consumers that schema-validate get a one-line update to accept the new keys, consumers that ignore unknown JSON keys (the dominant case) see no break at all. Phase C closes [`reference-design-remediation.md`](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) row 2.9 (outbound event envelope) and unblocks Phase D â€” the OverlappingZones processor needs the envelope to carry the `confidence` it computes. `src/tagpulse/integrations/signaling_envelope.py`, `src/tagpulse/integrations/webhook.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_envelope.py`, `tests/unit/test_webhook_envelope.py`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase B â€” signaling-rule kind filter, per-scope cap enforcement, periodic dispatcher shell, and `signaling.attribution_settled` topic (ADR-021 v2).** Plumbing-only slice â€” wires the schema landed in Phase A through the service, API, worker, and event-bus layers without changing evaluator behaviour. Real processor logic lands in Phase D; the outbound-envelope upgrade lands in Phase C. **B1 schema extensions** in [`src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py): per-trigger Pydantic config models (`SignalingPeriodicConfig` cadence_minutes 1..1440, `SignalingOnChangeConfig` min_delta+cooldown_s, `SignalingOnInactivityConfig` inactivity_minutes+cooldown_s, `SignalingOnInferenceConfig` min_confidenceâˆˆ[0,1], `SignalingOnEntryConfig` / `SignalingOnExitConfig` zone_id+optional subject_kinds, `SignalingOverlappingZonesProcessorConfig` aggregation_window_sâˆˆ{30,60,300,1800}); the `_SIGNALING_TRIGGER_CONFIGS` lookup table; the `validate_signaling_condition_config(condition_type, condition_config) -> BaseModel | None` helper that returns the parsed model for signaling condition_types, `None` for legacy, and raises `ValidationError` on a bad payload. `SIGNALING_DEFAULT_CAP_PER_SCOPE: int = 5` constant for the per-`(tenant_id, event_type, category_id)` active-signaling-rule cap. `RuleCreate` and `RuleUpdate` extended with the nine Phase A columns (`event_type`, `trigger`, `processor`, `confidence_threshold`, `category_ids`, `asset_label_filters`/`zone_label_filters`/`site_label_filters`, `integration_ids`); a `RuleCreate._signaling_columns_match_condition_type` model_validator auto-populates `event_type` and `trigger` from a `signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>` condition_type, rejects mismatched explicit values, and rejects signaling-only fields on legacy condition_types so a client can't smuggle a `category_ids=[â€¦]` onto a `threshold` rule. `RuleResponse` gets a computed `kind: Literal["legacy","signaling"]` populated by a model_validator (event_type None â†’ "legacy", else "signaling"); the validator overrides any caller-provided value so `kind` is always authoritative. **B1+B2 service** in [`src/tagpulse/rules/__init__.py`](src/tagpulse/rules/__init__.py): new `SignalingScopeCapExceededError(Exception)` carrying tenant_id, event_type, category_id, current_count, cap. `RulesService.create_rule(tenant_id, rule, *, allow_cap_override=False)` calls `validate_signaling_condition_config` then `_enforce_signaling_cap` (skipped on override). `RulesService.list_rules(tenant_id, *, enabled_only=False, kind=None)` filters via `RuleModel.event_type.is_(None)` for legacy / `.is_not(None)` for signaling â€” uses the existing `idx_rules_signaling_active` partial index from migration 040 for the signaling path. `RulesService.update_rule(tenant_id, rule_id, patch, *, allow_cap_override=False)` re-runs the cap when `event_type`/`category_ids`/`enabled` changes and re-runs the validator when `condition_type`/`condition_config` changes. `RulesService.count_active_signaling_rules_for_scope(tenant_id, event_type, category_id, *, exclude_rule_id)` uses `func.cardinality(RuleModel.category_ids) == 0` for the broadcast scope (`category_id IS NULL`) and the PG-idiomatic `literal(category_id) == any_(RuleModel.category_ids)` for a specific category â€” cleaner than `ARRAY.contains()` and avoids the pyright `Argument of type "list[UUID]" cannot be assigned` error. `_enforce_signaling_cap` raises `SignalingScopeCapExceededError` when count â‰¥ cap; legacy rules (event_type=None) and disabled rules short-circuit without invoking the counter. **B2 API routes** in [`src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py`](src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py): `POST /rules` and `PATCH /rules/{id}` gain `override: bool = Query(default=False)` (admin-only â€” editor passing `?override=true` returns 403 before any DB work); `SignalingScopeCapExceededError` is mapped to HTTP 409 with structured detail `{"error": "signaling_scope_cap_exceeded", "event_type", "category_id", "current_count", "cap", "override_hint"}`; admin-with-override that touches a signaling rule writes one `audit_logs` row per call via `AuditLogger(session=session).log(..., action="signaling.cap_override", resource_type="rule", resource_id=<rule.id>, changes={event_type, category_ids})`. `GET /rules` gains `kind: Literal["legacy","signaling"] | None = Query(default=None)` for the discriminator filter; omitting the param returns all rules (backwards-compatible). **B3 worker shell** â€” new module [`src/tagpulse/signaling/`](src/tagpulse/signaling/) with `PeriodicSignalingDispatcher` in [`src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`](src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py): mirrors the existing `InventoryRuleWorker` lifecycle (`start`/`stop`/`_loop`/`run_once`); reads cadence from `condition_config.cadence_minutes` (1..1440, validated); tracks in-memory `_last_fired: dict[UUID, datetime]` for cadence accounting; iterates active rules whose `condition_type` is one of `SIGNALING_PERIODIC_CONDITION_TYPES = ("signaling.location.periodic", "signaling.geolocation.periodic", "signaling.temperature.periodic")` via the new `RulesService.get_active_rules_by_condition_types_all_tenants(...)` helper. Phase B implementation of `_evaluate_periodic_rule` is a shell â€” it logs and records a `rule_evaluations` usage-meter tick but doesn't create alerts yet (Phase D adds the real processor pipeline). Worker is wired into the FastAPI lifespan in [`src/tagpulse/api/main.py`](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) behind `settings.workers_inline=True`, alongside the existing dwell_worker / inventory_worker; stored on `app.state.periodic_signaling_dispatcher`. **B4 event bus** â€” new `Topic.SIGNALING_ATTRIBUTION_SETTLED = "signaling.attribution_settled"` in [`src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py`](src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py), in-process (per ADR-010) for the upcoming attribution-settled fan-out the location/geolocation/temperature processors will publish in Phase D. **B5 tests** â€” four new test modules + ~30 new tests in `tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`, ~50 new tests total: [`tests/unit/test_signaling_event_bus.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_event_bus.py) (4 tests â€” enum value, list iteration for WebhookDispatcher discovery, end-to-end publish+subscribe with `AsyncEventBus(capacity=100, overflow="raise")`, multi-subscriber fan-out); [`tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py) (9 tests â€” condition_types match ADR; empty rules no-op; first tick fires all three rule types; second tick within cadence skips; tick after cadence elapsed fires + advances last_fired; multiple cadences independent; invalid cadence_minutes skipped with warning; evaluator hook records meter tick; start/stop lifecycle); [`tests/unit/test_signaling_rule_service.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_rule_service.py) (15 tests covering cap enforcement at 4/5/6, legacy skip, disabled skip, broadcast scope, multi-category any-over-cap rejection, create_rule cap-check invocation, override bypass, invalid-config rejection before cap, legacy create unchanged, update enable re-checks cap, update override bypasses, list_rules SQL shape for kind=signaling/legacy/none); [`tests/unit/test_signaling_rules_api.py`](tests/unit/test_signaling_rules_api.py) (10 tests via FastAPI + ASGITransport + dependency_overrides covering GET ?kind=signaling/legacy/none/bogus, POST 409 detail shape, POST override admin-only 403, POST admin override 201 + audit row, POST override on legacy rule no audit, PATCH 409, PATCH admin override 200 + audit row). **`make check` clean**: 963 unit tests passing (+~50 from Phase A baseline), `ruff check` âœ“, `mypy` âœ“ (no issues in source files). No behaviour change for existing rules â€” the new fields default to None / empty / 0.0 / False so pre-Phase-B rules round-trip identically; the cap only applies to rules where `event_type IS NOT NULL`. Phase B is the gate to Phase C (envelope upgrade) and Phase D (real processor logic). `src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/rules/__init__.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/rules.py`, `src/tagpulse/events/protocol.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/__init__.py`, `src/tagpulse/signaling/periodic_dispatcher.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_event_bus.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_periodic_dispatcher.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_rule_service.py`, `tests/unit/test_signaling_rules_api.py`.

- **Sprint 41 Phase A â€” schema + Pydantic foundation for Configurable Signaling Events (ADR-021 v2).** Lays the groundwork for the rest of Sprint 41 by landing the additive schema + the discriminator helper the evaluator (Phase B), envelope (Phase C), and API (Phase E) will all build on. **Migration `040_rules_signaling_events.py`** extends `rules` with nine additive columns â€” `event_type VARCHAR(32) NULL`, `trigger VARCHAR(32) NULL`, `processor VARCHAR(32) NULL`, `confidence_threshold NUMERIC(3,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0.0`, `category_ids UUID[] NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'`, `asset_label_filters JSONB NULL`, `zone_label_filters JSONB NULL`, `site_label_filters JSONB NULL`, `integration_ids UUID[] NULL` â€” all nullable or defaulted so existing rows survive untouched; `event_type IS NULL` is the implicit `kind = legacy` discriminator the API + UI use to keep the new "Signaling Events" namespace separate from pre-existing rules. Plus partial index `idx_rules_signaling_active ON rules (tenant_id, event_type, trigger) WHERE enabled = true AND event_type IS NOT NULL` that keeps the upcoming evaluator's hot path narrow (only currently-enabled signaling rules show up â€” no full table scan on a tenant that has thousands of legacy rules and zero signaling rules yet). `trigger` is a non-reserved keyword in PostgreSQL so the column does not need quoting; matches ADR-021 verbatim. `RuleModel` in [`src/tagpulse/models/database.py`](src/tagpulse/models/database.py) mirrors the migration with proper types (`Decimal` for `confidence_threshold`, `ARRAY(UUID(as_uuid=True))` for the two UUID arrays â€” first use of `ARRAY` in the codebase), all with server-defaults matching the migration so SQLAlchemy and Postgres agree on the default values. **Pydantic foundation** in [`src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`](src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py): `_RULE_CONDITION_PATTERN` regex extended with the 12 new `signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>` values, each `(event_type, trigger)` pair listed explicitly so impossible combinations like `signaling.temperature.on_entry` reject at parse time rather than reaching the evaluator. New `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS: dict[str, frozenset[str]]` constant is the authoritative map of which triggers are legal for each event type (`location` gets all 4 non-spatial triggers including `on_inference`; `geolocation` and `temperature` get the same minus `on_inference`; `geofencing` gets only `on_entry` / `on_exit` â€” entry/exit are spatial primitives that don't apply to subject-bound metric streams, and `on_inference` only makes sense for location attribution). `SIGNALING_PROCESSORS: ("isolated_zones", "overlapping_zones")` constant for symmetric lookup. New `split_signaling_condition_type(condition_type: str) -> tuple[str, str] | None` helper is the in-process discriminator the upcoming evaluator + service will use to route a rule's condition_type to its (event_type, trigger) handlers without re-parsing strings â€” returns `None` for legacy `condition_type` values, signaling-shaped-but-invalid pairs (the regex would also reject these before they reach the helper, but the helper is defensive), and malformed inputs; the tuple-returning case is guaranteed to be one of the 12 valid pairs in `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS`. **Tests**: 51 new unit tests in [`tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`](tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py) â€” `TestSignalingConditionTypes` parametrizes all 12 valid pairs through `RuleCreate` (asserts each is accepted), a fail-list of 16 invalid pairs (cross-product errors like `signaling.temperature.on_entry`, made-up event types like `signaling.humidity.on_change`, wrong namespace depth like `signaling.location.on_change.extra`, wrong prefix like `signal.location.on_change`), a regression guard ensuring all 10 legacy `condition_type` values still validate, and a `test_twelve_pairs_is_the_full_matrix` count-check that trips if the regex and `SIGNALING_VALID_PAIRS` ever drift apart; `TestSplitSignalingConditionType` parametrizes the 12 valid pairs through the helper (asserts each returns the expected tuple) plus a 10-case fail-list (legacy types return None, signaling-shaped-but-invalid returns None, wrong shape / empty string return None). Full unit suite delta: +51 tests; `python -m pytest tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py` â†’ 58 passed (was 7). **Docs**: [`docs/data-models.md`](docs/data-models.md) Â§"rules" table updated with the nine new columns + the `idx_rules_signaling_active` partial-index note + Migration column updated to "006 (initial), 040 (Sprint 41 signaling-event columns + partial index)"; `condition_type` Notes column updated from the stale "threshold, absence, rate_change" to spell out "10 legacy values â€¦ + 12 signaling values (`signaling.<event_type>.<trigger>`) per ADR-021 v2"; new `signaling.*.periodic` condition-config example added under #### Condition config shapes (cadence_minutes + processor_config nested block). **Terminology note**: this PR also renames `sensing` â†’ `signaling` throughout the new Phase A code + ADR-021 v2 content + Sprint 41 roadmap plan, aligning with Azure-Monitor's "Signal â†’ Condition â†’ Action" vocabulary that the deferred Sprint 4X taxonomy-cleanup ADR will ratify. The ADR file path (`docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`) stays for link stability; the title + body are updated. Historical CHANGELOG entries (PR #45, #51, vendor-neutrality sweep) that reference "Sensing Events" are intentionally left as-is â€” they describe shipped work as-written. **Out of scope for this slice (still part of Sprint 41 Phase A, follow-up commits on this PR)**: full Pydantic discriminated-union BaseModel per trigger (`SignalingPeriodicConfig`, `SignalingOverlappingZonesProcessorConfig`) â€” deferred to Phase B where the evaluator actually consumes them; integration test for migration round-trip + index predicate verification â€” covered by the existing `tests/integration/test_migration_round_trip.py` harness via `make migration-check` (requires a TimescaleDB container so it's CI-gated, not part of `make check`). No behaviour change yet â€” the new columns are additive and nothing reads them until Phase B lands the evaluator. `migrations/versions/040_rules_signaling_events.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/rule_schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_rule_schemas.py`, `docs/data-models.md`, `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md`, `docs/roadmap.md`.

- **`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md` â€” Sprint 39 row 2.2a flipped Commit â†’ âœ… Done.** ADR 020 Phase B orphan `entity_labels` cleanup landed in [#47 `7ce3292`](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/commit/7ce3292) per the previous Sprint 39 bullet (the slice that wired `TimescaleLabelRepository.delete_for_entity` into the three hard-delete repository methods for sites, zones, and categories). Â§3.1 row 2.2a Status column updated from **ðŸŸ  Commit (in flight, #47)** to **âœ… Done ([#47](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/47), `7ce3292`) / 39**; Notes column unchanged (still spells out the polymorphic-FK reason that `count_associations()` overcounts when orphans exist, and the soft-delete vs hard-delete split that makes assets and devices intentionally exempt). - **Sprint 39 â€” ADR 020 Phase B: orphan `entity_labels` cleanup on hard-delete entity handlers (row 2.2a).** Closes the lone unshipped clause of ADR 020 â€” "Orphan cleanup happens in the entity-delete handlers (Phase B)" â€” that survived the Sprint 35 Phases A/C/D/E ship train. The problem: sites, zones, and categories hard-delete via `await self._session.delete(row)` in [`src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/sites_zones.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/sites_zones.py) and [`src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/categories.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/categories.py) with no cleanup of the polymorphic `entity_labels` rows that pointed at them. The `entity_labels` table holds a regular `label_id` FK to `labels` (`ON DELETE RESTRICT` per the ADR / Phase A) but **only a polymorphic `entity_id`** to the owning entity (no FK â€” couldn't have one because the same column targets five different tables), so the entity-delete path leaves the association rows behind as dangling pointers. `count_associations()` on the parent label (in [`labels.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py)) cannot join the entity table for tenant scope â€” that join is impossible for the polymorphic case â€” so orphan rows are indistinguishable from live ones and **inflate the count permanently**. Concrete user-visible failure mode: an admin deletes the three sites that were all tagged `priority=p1`, then tries to delete the now-unused `priority` label via `DELETE /labels/{id}`, and gets back `409 Conflict { "message": "Label â€¦ still has 3 association(s)", "association_count": 3 }` even though `GET /sites?labels[priority]=p1` returns the empty array. The 409 is unresolvable from the UI because `GET /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` looks up by `(entity_type, entity_id)` and the operator has no way to discover which dead `entity_id`s the orphan rows point at. The fix adds `TimescaleLabelRepository.delete_for_entity(tenant_id, entity_type, entity_id) -> int` (placed alongside the existing `disassociate` method since it's the catalog-table sibling) that runs a tenant-scoped JOIN-then-delete: `SELECT entity_labels WHERE entity_labels.entity_id = :eid JOIN labels ON labels.tenant_id = :tid AND labels.entity_type = :etype` and then `session.delete(row)` per match, returning the row count for audit/observability. Tenant scoping is done via the JOIN to `labels.tenant_id` rather than a bare `DELETE â€¦ WHERE entity_id = â€¦` because the association table has no `tenant_id` column of its own â€” matching the rest of the module's tenant-scoping pattern (`disassociate`, `count_associations`, `get_association`). The new method is wired into the three hard-delete repository methods *before* `await self._session.delete(row)` is called, so the cleanup and the entity delete are in the same transaction and either both happen or neither does. Order: (1) `TimescaleSiteRepository.delete` â€” call `delete_for_entity(tenant_id, "site", site_id)` between the existing `select â€¦ scalar_one_or_none()` and `session.delete(row)`; cache invalidation unchanged. (2) `TimescaleZoneRepository.delete` â€” same pattern with `"zone"`; `_geofence_cache_invalidate(tenant_id)` still runs after the flush. (3) `TimescaleCategoryRepository.delete` â€” same pattern with `"category"`, placed *after* the existing `CategoryInUseError` guard (which protects against asset references, not label references â€” a category with labels but zero assets used to fall through to a successful delete that leaked labels; now it cleans up properly). Asset and device hard deletes do not exist â€” assets soft-delete to `status='retired'` via `TimescaleAssetRepository.delete` and devices soft-delete via `POST /devices/{id}/decommission`. Both are **intentionally** unchanged because soft-delete keeps the entity row alive, label associations remain valid (and historically useful: a retired asset still shows its tagged `building=warehouse-a` location for audit purposes), and the row's `status` discriminator means the entity won't appear in default list queries anyway. The `delete_for_entity` method is a no-op (returns 0, skips the flush) when the entity had no labels â€” the cheap path for the common case. The module docstring in [`labels.py`](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py) is updated to mention `delete_for_entity` in the association-methods list with a cross-reference to the calling sites. **Tests:** new [`tests/unit/test_orphan_label_cleanup.py`](tests/unit/test_orphan_label_cleanup.py) (4 tests) pins the contract for the three hard-delete repository methods using an in-memory `_RecordingSession` that captures every `execute` / `delete` / `flush` in order so the test can assert (a) `TimescaleSiteRepository.delete` issues two SELECTs (entity lookup + orphan SELECT) before the `session.delete(row)`, with the orphan SELECT compiling to SQL containing `from entity_labels`, `join labels`, `labels.tenant_id`, and `labels.entity_type`; (b) when the entity SELECT returns `None` the orphan cleanup is **skipped entirely** (no second execute, no delete) and `delete()` returns `False` â€” defends against a regression that would run an orphan SELECT against a tenant the caller doesn't actually own a row in; (c) `TimescaleZoneRepository.delete` follows the same contract with the orphan SELECT containing `labels.entity_type` and `entity_labels.entity_id`; (d) `TimescaleCategoryRepository.delete` runs three SELECTs in the right order â€” `count_referencing_assets` first (which raises `CategoryInUseError` and short-circuits the rest if the count is non-zero), then category lookup, then orphan cleanup â€” before the `session.delete(row)` and the `flush`. Plus 4 new repository-level tests in [`tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py`](tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py) under a new `TestDeleteForEntity` class: (1) `test_select_is_tenant_scoped_via_labels_join` compiles the SELECT and asserts `join labels`, `labels.tenant_id`, `labels.entity_type`, and `entity_labels.entity_id` all appear (regression guard against a future refactor that drops the JOIN and tries to use a bare `tenant_id` predicate that doesn't exist on `entity_labels`); (2) `test_returns_zero_when_no_orphans` confirms the empty-result path returns 0 and skips the `flush()` (cheap path matters because most entity deletes will have zero labels â€” paying a transaction flush per empty cleanup would matter under load); (3) `test_deletes_each_row_and_flushes_once` confirms multiple rows are deleted individually via `session.delete(row)` (so SQLAlchemy's identity map sees each removal â€” important if anything else in the same transaction touches `entity_labels`) but `flush()` runs exactly once; (4) `test_predicates_bind_entity_type_and_id` compiles with `literal_binds=True` and asserts the entity_type literal and entity_id UUID both appear in the compiled SQL string (defends against accidental string coercion or predicate drop). The shared `_CapturingSession` helper in `test_labels_repository.py` mirrors the dialect-compile pattern already established by `tests/unit/test_assets_repository_filters.py` (Sprint 37 row 2.8a) â€” no Postgres needed, compiles against the postgres dialect via `sqlalchemy.dialects.postgresql`. Full unit suite: 821 passed + 1 skipped (was 817 + 1 before; +4 in `test_labels_repository.py`, new file `test_orphan_label_cleanup.py` adds 4). `make check` clean: `ruff check` âœ“, `mypy` âœ“ (no issues in 103 source files). **Doc updates**: new row 2.2a in Â§3.1 of [`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) tracks the slice (Severity ðŸŸ , Decision **Commit (in flight, #47)**) with the full failure-mode explainer and call-site list; row 2.2 itself is untouched (remains âœ… Done â€” the original five-PR ship train still owns Phases A/C/D/E and that decision didn't change).
