- **Sprint 35 Phase E â€” Labels docs + remediation flip.** Closes out the Sprint 35 backend story by documenting the labels surface for end users and updating the scope-lock doc to reflect what shipped. New `## Labels` section in [`docs/user-guide.md`](docs/user-guide.md) (between **Inventory** and **Tenant Settings**, with a matching TOC entry) covers the four things an operator actually needs to know: (1) where labels sit relative to Categories (the single primary-classification slot on assets) and the `metadata` JSONB escape hatch (long blobs, structured nested data, integration-specific payloads); (2) the two-level catalog + associations model â€” a catalog row defines what `key` can exist for a given `entity_type`, an association attaches a `(key, value)` pair to a specific entity instance, and the same `key` is independent across entity types so `location` on Assets and `location` on Sites don't collide; (3) the eight tenant-scoped endpoints with explicit role gates per row (`GET /labels` viewer+, `POST/PATCH /labels` editor/admin, `DELETE /labels/{id}` admin-only with `409 + association_count`; `GET /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` viewer+, `POST` editor/admin with `409 + cap:30`, `DELETE` editor/admin) â€” the URL segment is plural (`assets`/`sites`/`zones`/`devices`/`categories`) per the existing REST convention and lookup happens by `(tenant, entity_type, lower(key))` so clients never need to know the synthetic catalog UUID to attach a value; (4) the deep-object `?labels[KEY]=V1,V2` filter on `GET /assets`/`/sites`/`/zones`/`/devices` with worked examples from ADR 020 (single pair, multi-key AND, comma-separated OR within a key, the four-key combined form), the AND-across-keys-OR-within-values semantics spelled out, the three guard rails repeated verbatim (â‰¤ 5 distinct keys/request, â‰¤ 20 values/key, value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$`), the explicit rejection of the repeated-parallel `?label.key=X&label.value=Y` form (query-param order isn't guaranteed across middleware), and a tagging-a-Boston-asset walkthrough showing `curl` invocations for catalog create â†’ association attach â†’ filtered list with `--data-urlencode` for the `[`/`]` characters. Format rules table reproduces the key regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$`, value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$`, optional `#RRGGBB` color, case-insensitive key uniqueness per `(tenant, entity_type)`, and the 30-per-entity cap with its dual API + DB trigger enforcement. The five audit-log event names emitted on every mutation (`label.created`, `label.updated` only when `_diff` is non-empty, `label.deleted`, `label.associated`, `label.disassociated`) are cross-linked from the existing **Audit Log** section's preset filters. [`docs/operator-quickstart.md`](docs/operator-quickstart.md) is **intentionally untouched** â€” that doc is strictly operations (deploys, alert routing, on-call triage cheat-sheet) and labels are a feature surface, not an operational concern; bolting on a Pointers-section link just to tick the original Phase E checklist would have been bookkeeping noise. [`docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md`](docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md) row 2.2 (Labels first-class) flipped **Commit â†’ âœ… Done** with all four implementing PRs and short SHAs ([#36](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/36) `fd38046` kickoff Â· [#37](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/37) `c5db1a7` schema Â· [#38](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/38) `fe0b732` API Â· [#39](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/39) `4493a02` filter) per the doc's own Â§7 "Updating this document" rule; row 3.9 (Asset Detail Events Log tab + Labels chips) **stays Commit** because the chips half is UI work in TagPulse-UI that hasn't shipped, but gains an annotation that the backend prerequisites are now in place (links back to row 2.2) so the chip PR isn't blocked on more backend work. - **Sprint 35 Phase C â€” Labels deep-object filter (ADR 020).** Lights up the `?labels[KEY]=V1,V2` filter on the four entity list endpoints (`GET /assets`, `GET /sites`, `GET /zones`, `GET /devices`) that Phase B intentionally deferred. New module `src/tagpulse/api/label_filter.py` exposes two purpose-built primitives. (1) `parse_label_filter(query_params)` â€” pure parser over Starlette's `QueryParams.multi_items()` so duplicate `labels[KEY]=â€¦` entries on the same request merge correctly; returns `dict[str, list[str]] | None` (`None` when no `labels[...]` keys are present so the call site can short-circuit), raises `LabelFilterError(ValueError)` on any guard-rail violation. Guard rails mirror ADR 020 Â§"Filter encoding" verbatim: â‰¤ 5 distinct keys/request (`LABEL_FILTER_MAX_KEYS`), â‰¤ 20 values/key (`LABEL_FILTER_MAX_VALUES_PER_KEY`), key regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$` and value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` (imported from `schemas.py` so the catalog and the filter can't drift), and any empty segment â€” leading comma, trailing comma, double comma, or fully-empty `labels[k]=` â€” rejects with `"Empty value â€¦"` rather than silently matching nothing. Keys fold to lowercase so `labels[Location]=` and `labels[location]=` merge into one bucket (matches the catalog's `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` functional unique index from migration 039); values stay case-sensitive. (2) `apply_label_filter(stmt, *, tenant_id, entity_type, entity_id_col, labels)` â€” pure SQLAlchemy applicator that appends one correlated `EXISTS` per key onto the caller's `Select`, joining `entity_labels â†’ labels` and binding `LabelModel.tenant_id = :tid AND LabelModel.entity_type = :et AND lower(LabelModel.key) = lower(:key) AND EntityLabelModel.value IN (:v1, :v2, â€¦)`. Tenant scoping is enforced inside the EXISTS â€” a guess-the-UUID attack on another tenant's label can't bypass the `tenant_id` check on the join side. The four list routes now accept `request: Request`, run the parser, surface `LabelFilterError` as a 400, and pass `labels=` through their service. Service signatures (`AssetService.list_assets`, `SiteZoneService.list_sites` / `.list_zones`, `DeviceService.list_devices`) gained the `labels: dict[str, list[str]] | None = None` kwarg (default `None` preserves existing call sites). Repository `.list()` methods on `TimescaleAssetRepository`, the site + zone repos, and `TimescaleDeviceRepository` now invoke `apply_label_filter` between their existing per-field WHEREs and the `ORDER BY / LIMIT / OFFSET` tail. `DeviceRepository` Protocol updated to mirror the new kwarg. **Why the manual `Request.query_params` parse instead of a typed FastAPI `Query` parameter:** OpenAPI 3.0 supports `style: deepObject, explode: true` (which is what ADR 020 specifies) but FastAPI's `Query()` machinery doesn't surface deep-object query params as a single typed value â€” the `[`/`]` characters in the param name aren't legal Python identifiers and Pydantic v2 won't bind them. Going through `request.query_params.multi_items()` keeps the route signature clean, lets the guard-rail errors return a real 400 with a useful message, and crucially **does not change the generated `openapi.json`** (the spec gate stays green without manual schema patches â€” verified locally). **AND across keys, OR within values** is the SQL contract: each key adds one `EXISTS`, and within an EXISTS the value list compiles to `entity_labels.value IN (â€¦)` â€” equivalent to the ADR's example SQL. Performance shape is index-friendly: each `EXISTS` is a fast probe via `entity_labels(label_id, entity_id)` PK + `labels(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` functional unique index. **Tests:** 50 new unit tests in `tests/unit/test_label_filter.py` cover parser happy-path (single pair, multi-key AND, comma-split OR, the four-key combined form from the ADR), duplicate-key merge, dedup-within-key, key case-folding, the full guard-rail matrix (max keys + at-max accepted, max values + at-max accepted, parametrised key + value regex with allowed and disallowed inputs, empty/leading/trailing/double comma all rejected), `apply_label_filter` pass-through for `None` and `{}`, and SQL-shape assertions (compile against the postgres dialect with `literal_binds=True` so the test reads what the DB actually sees: one EXISTS per key, `entity_type` bound to the singular form, key bound lowercased). The existing fake repositories in `tests/unit/test_device_service.py` and `tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py` picked up the new `labels=` kwarg (accepted-but-ignored at the fake layer â€” repository-level SQL behaviour is covered in the new test module). Full unit suite now 807 tests (+50 from Phase B's 757). `src/tagpulse/api/label_filter.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/assets.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/devices.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/sites_zones.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/services/asset_service.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/services/device_service.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/services/sites_zones_service.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/protocols.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/assets.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/devices.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/sites_zones.py`, `tests/unit/test_label_filter.py`, `tests/unit/test_device_service.py`, `tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py`.

- **Sprint 35 Phase B â€” Labels API (ADR 020).** Builds the catalog + per-entity association REST surface on top of the Phase A schema. **Pydantic schemas** in `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py` add `LabelEntityType` (`Literal["asset","site","zone","device","category"]`, lockstep with the migration 039 `CHECK` literal list), `LabelCreate` (`entity_type` + `key` + optional `color`), `LabelUpdate` (`key` / `color` only â€” `entity_type` is intentionally absent because ADR 020 declares it immutable), `LabelResponse` (full row inc. `created_by` / `updated_by` opaque JWT UUIDs), `LabelAssociationCreate` (`key` + `value`; the repository looks up the catalog row by `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` rather than requiring the client to know the synthetic UUID), and `LabelAssociationResponse` (joined view carrying `entity_type` / `key` / `color` alongside the polymorphic `entity_id`). All regex patterns mirror the DB `CHECK` constraints exactly â€” `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$` for keys, `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` for values (hyphen-included per the Phase A contradiction fix), `^#[0-9A-Fa-f]{6}$` for colours. **TimescaleDB repository** in `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py` (`TimescaleLabelRepository`) provides `list_for_tenant` / `get` / `find_by_key` / `create` / `update` / `count_associations` / `delete` for the catalog, plus `list_for_entity` / `get_association` / `associate` / `disassociate` for the per-entity surface. Domain exceptions (`LabelKeyConflictError` extends `ValueError`; `LabelInUseError` and `LabelCapExceededError` extend `RuntimeError`) replace raw `IntegrityError` so the route layer doesn't have to know about SQLSTATEs. A pure `_pg_sqlstate(exc)` helper normalises asyncpg's `.sqlstate` and psycopg2's `.pgcode` so the same error mapping works under either driver; mapped codes are `23505` â†’ `LabelKeyConflictError` (functional unique index on `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` or composite PK collision on `entity_labels`) and `23514` â†’ `LabelCapExceededError` (raised by the `trg_enforce_label_cap` BEFORE INSERT trigger on the 31st row per entity). `LabelCapExceededError.CAP = 30` is asserted in tests so any future cap bump trips the unit suite if the migration and the constant drift. Tenant scoping on the polymorphic `entity_labels` side is enforced by joining through `labels` on every read and delete â€” never by `label_id` alone â€” so a guess-the-UUID attack on another tenant cannot disassociate their rows. **Routes** in `src/tagpulse/api/routes/labels.py` ship eight endpoints per ADR 020 Â§"API path deviation": `GET /labels?entity_type=` (viewer+), `POST /labels` (editor/admin), `GET /labels/{id}` (viewer+), `PATCH /labels/{id}` (editor/admin; 400 if the payload smuggles `entity_type`), `DELETE /labels/{id}` (admin only; 409 with `{"message": ..., "association_count": N}` if in use), `GET /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` (viewer+), `POST /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels` (editor/admin; 404 if the key isn't in the catalog, 409 with `{"message": ..., "cap": 30}` on cap, 409 on duplicate), and `DELETE /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels/{label_id}` (editor/admin). The URL segment is the **plural** form (`assets` / `sites` / `zones` / `devices` / `categories`) per the existing REST convention; an `_ENTITY_TYPE_FROM_URL` mapping bridges to the singular DB value, and an unknown segment returns 404 ("Unknown entity kind") before any DB work happens. A `_diff(before, after)` helper builds the audit `changes` dict over the `key` / `color` field pair only (mirrors the Categories pattern); `updated_at` is intentionally excluded so a no-op PATCH doesn't write a noise audit row. **Audit log events** emitted via `AuditLogger(session=session).log(...)`: `label.created`, `label.updated` (only when `_diff` is non-empty), `label.deleted`, `label.associated`, `label.disassociated`. **OTel counter** `tagpulse_labels_associations_total{tenant_id, entity_type}` added to `src/tagpulse/core/otel_metrics.py` and incremented on every successful `POST /{entity_segment}/{id}/labels`, so dashboards can spot tenants approaching the 30-per-entity cap or track tag-driven inventory growth per entity kind. **Router wiring** in `src/tagpulse/api/main.py` adds `labels_router` import (alphabetical, between `inventory_imports_router` and `metrics_router`) and the matching `app.include_router(labels_router)` at the end of the include block (after Categories). **Tests**: 64 schema tests in `tests/unit/test_labels_schemas.py` cover `LabelCreate` (entity-type enum, key length / regex parametrised across allowed + disallowed chars, color hex validation), `LabelUpdate` (empty-payload accepted, `entity_type` not in `model_fields`, `exclude_unset=True` keeps explicit `color=None` clearable), `LabelAssociationCreate` (value length / regex, hyphen accepted per the Phase A contradiction fix), `LabelAssociationResponse` (kwargs round-trip), and `_diff` (no-change â†’ empty, single-field changes, both-field changes, explicit clear-to-null); 12 repository-helper tests in `tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py` cover `_pg_sqlstate` (asyncpg `.sqlstate` vs psycopg2 `.pgcode`, both-present preference, none-present return), the three domain exceptions (class hierarchy, payload, `CAP=30` constant), parametrised across the three classes. Full unit suite now 757 tests (+76 from Phase A's 681). The deep-object `?labels[KEY]=V1,V2` filter on `/assets` / `/sites` / `/zones` / `/devices` is deliberately deferred to Phase C â€” it's cross-cutting across four routers + four services + four repositories, and warrants its own focused review window. `src/tagpulse/models/schemas.py`, `src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/labels.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/routes/labels.py`, `src/tagpulse/api/main.py`, `src/tagpulse/core/otel_metrics.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_schemas.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_repository.py`.

- **Sprint 35 Phase A â€” Labels catalog schema (ADR 020).** Migration `039_labels_catalog.py` introduces two tenant-scoped tables. (1) `labels` â€” catalog of label *keys* scoped to one `entity_type` (`asset` / `site` / `zone` / `device` / `category`); functional UNIQUE index on `(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` enforces case-insensitive uniqueness per entity-type slot (so `location` on Sites and `location` on Assets are independent). DB-side CHECK constraints enforce the `entity_type` enum, the key regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.+$]{3,24}$`, and the optional `color` regex `^#[0-9A-Fa-f]{6}$`. (2) `entity_labels` â€” polymorphic association `(label_id, entity_id, value)`; `label_id` FK is **`ON DELETE RESTRICT`** so deleting a catalog row that's still referenced returns 409 + `association_count` at the API layer (matches the Categories pattern from ADR 019, *not* the CASCADE the original ADR draft showed). `entity_id` has no FK â€” it points polymorphically at `assets` / `sites` / `zones` / `devices` / `categories` rows; orphan cleanup happens in the entity-delete handlers in Phase B, not in the DB. Value regex is `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` (hyphen added vs the ADR draft so `warehouse-a` style values actually validate; matches k8s/AWS/GCP tag value conventions). A `enforce_label_cap()` PL/pgSQL function + `BEFORE INSERT` trigger backstops the 30-labels-per-entity cap; SQLSTATE `23514` surfaces as a 409 in the API. RLS is enabled on both tables (theatre-only per the repo convention; the app filters explicitly by `tenant_id` in every query). `LabelModel` + `EntityLabelModel` ORM classes in `src/tagpulse/models/database.py` mirror the migration; `created_by` / `updated_by` are plain `UUID NULL` columns without an FK (no `users` table in TagPulse â€” auth is JWT-based, mirrors `audit_logs.user_id` from migration 015). 16 new unit tests in `tests/unit/test_labels_models.py` introspect the ORM shape so anyone editing the migration without touching the models (or vice versa) trips a fast unit test before the integration suite runs. Three contradictions in the merged ADR 020 are fixed alongside the schema that crystallizes them: (a) `ON DELETE CASCADE` â†’ `ON DELETE RESTRICT` (consistent with the 409 spec in the Â§"API path deviation" section), (b) value regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_.]{1,64}$` â†’ `^[A-Za-z0-9._-]{1,64}$` (so the Â§"Filter encoding" `warehouse-a` examples validate), (c) `created_by/updated_by UUID REFERENCES users(id)` â†’ `UUID` (no FK; no `users` table exists). The original `/v1/tenants/{slug}/...` API surface block in the ADR is now explicitly labelled "superseded by Â§'API path deviation' below" so future readers don't think two endpoint shapes were specified. `migrations/versions/039_labels_catalog.py`, `src/tagpulse/models/database.py`, `tests/unit/test_labels_models.py`, `docs/adr/020-labels-first-class.md`.

- **Sprint 35 kickoff â€” ADR 020 Labels first-class ratified.** Status flipped **Proposed â†’ Accepted** at the start of the implementing sprint. The three Open Questions are now closed inline: (Q1) `entity_type` is a `CHECK` constraint with a literal list (`'asset','site','zone','device','category'`) â€” matches the Categories `category_type` precedent in ADR 019, avoids enum-add-value migrations later; (Q2) pre-seeded common keys (`location`, `owner`, `priority`) are **deferred** until one cycle of operator UX feedback on the chip UI; (Q3) cross-entity label propagation is **out of scope** for this ADR (separate follow-up if a customer asks; the `entity_labels` shape doesn't preclude it). Added a Â§"API path deviation" subsection capturing that shipped paths are `/labels` + `/{entity_type}/{id}/labels` rather than the original `/v1/tenants/{slug}/...` draft (matches the Categories deviation in ADR 019). Added a Â§"Filter encoding" subsection specifying that label-based filters on existing list endpoints (`GET /assets`, `/sites`, `/zones`, `/devices`) use **OpenAPI `style: deepObject, explode: true`** with semantics **AND across distinct keys, OR within comma-separated values of the same key** (e.g. `?labels[location]=warehouse-a,warehouse-b&labels[priority]=high`). Same shape as Prometheus/Loki/Grafana label selectors. Guard rails: â‰¤ 5 distinct keys/request, â‰¤ 20 values/key, each value matches `^[A-Za-z0-9_.]{1,64}$`. Repeated-parallel `?label.key=X&label.value=Y` form is explicitly rejected (query-param order not guaranteed across middleware). SQL shape is one correlated `EXISTS` per key, fast via the existing `entity_labels(label_id, entity_id)` PK + `labels(tenant_id, entity_type, lower(key))` unique index. The cap-30 `BEFORE INSERT` trigger backstop got concrete `enforce_label_cap()` plpgsql in the schema block. Â§2 of `docs/design/reference-design-remediation.md` now marks Sprint 35 as **ðŸŸ¡ in flight** linking [#36](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/pull/36); rows 2.2 + 3.9 (chips half) will flip to âœ… Done per Â§7 when the implementing PR merges. `docs/adr/020-labels-first-class.md`.

- **Sprint 34 sites structured-address + Site/Transporter discriminator (gap 2.7).** Adds the Site vs. Transporter distinction and the geolocation + structured-address columns required by the Locations UI redesign. Alembic migration `038_sites_structured.py` adds `sites.kind VARCHAR(16) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'site'` with `CHECK (kind IN ('site','transporter'))`, `latitude` / `longitude` DOUBLE PRECISION with per-axis range CHECKs **and** an `ck_sites_latlon_paired` both-or-neither invariant, and `street_line1` / `street_line2` / `city` / `region` / `postal_code` / `country` (CHAR(2) with `~ '^[A-Z]{2}$'` CHECK for ISO 3166-1 alpha-2). Existing rows backfill to `kind='site'`; lat/lon and structured-address columns are nullable so the migration is online and zero-downtime. The legacy free-form `sites.address` TEXT column is **retained this release as a compatibility shadow** (mirrors the Sprint 34 categories `assets.asset_type` precedent â€” drop in a later migration once UI + clients have switched). `SiteCreate` / `SiteUpdate` gain matching fields with Pydantic validators: lat in `[-90, 90]` and lon in `[-180, 180]` (via `Field(ge=â€¦, le=â€¦)`), `country` normalised to uppercase ISO alpha-2 via a `mode="before"` `field_validator` (so whitespace and casing are tolerated before length checks fire), a `model_validator` that enforces the lat/lon paired invariant on `SiteCreate` and on `SiteUpdate` *only when both fields appear in the patch payload* (partial updates defer to the DB CHECK so the PATCH ergonomics stay clean), and a second `model_validator` on `SiteUpdate` that rejects explicit `null` for the NOT-NULL columns `name` / `kind` / `default_timezone` at 422 so the DB never sees the NULL and returns 500. `SiteModel.country` uses `CHAR(2)` to mirror the migration. `SiteResponse` and the TimescaleDB repository plumb all new fields through; the existing `update()` path needs no change because it already dispatches via `model_dump(exclude_unset=True)` + `setattr`. 34 new schema tests in `tests/unit/test_sites_structured_schemas.py` cover the kind enum, lat/lon range + paired logic for create + patch, country normalisation, a full-payload round-trip, and the explicit-null rejection (parametrized across `name` / `kind` / `default_timezone`, plus regression coverage that omission stays legal and nullable columns remain clearable); the existing `_site()` fixture in `tests/unit/test_sites_zones_service.py` extended with the new defaults so the 10 service-level tests still pass.
- **Sprint 34 Categories backend â€” ADR 019 ratified.** Categories become a first-class tenant-scoped entity (gap 2.1 of the reference-design audit). New `categories` table via Alembic migration `037_categories.py` with `UNIQUE(tenant_id, name)`, `CHECK` on `category_type IN ('liquid_container','reference_tag','rti_container','object')`, `CHECK` on `required_tags >= 1`, RLS policy `tenant_isolation_categories`, and a backfill that creates one `category_type='object'` row per distinct `(tenant_id, asset_type)` already in `assets`. `assets` gains a nullable `category_id` FK (`ON DELETE RESTRICT`) backfilled to the matching new category by name; `assets.asset_type` is kept this release as a compatibility shadow (per ADR â€” drop in a later migration once UI + clients have switched). New router `src/tagpulse/api/routes/categories.py` exposes `GET /categories` (viewer+), `POST /categories` (editor/admin), `GET /categories/{id}` (viewer+), `PATCH /categories/{id}` (editor/admin; rejects `category_type` mutation with 400 â€” immutability is API-enforced per the ADR), and `DELETE /categories/{id}` (admin; 409 with `asset_count` payload if any asset still references it). All mutations audited (`category.created` / `category.updated` / `category.deleted`). Routes use the established current-tenant scoping pattern (`Depends(get_current_tenant)`) rather than the `/v1/tenants/{slug}/â€¦` paths drafted in ADR 019 â€” see the route docstring for the deviation. ADR 019 status flipped Proposed â†’ Accepted. `docs/adr/019-categories.md`.
- **`installer` user role (gap 2.6).** Joins the existing `admin` / `editor` / `viewer` set on `UserCreate` / `UserUpdate`. Pydantic-only change â€” the underlying `users.role` column is `String(50)` with no DB-level constraint. No new `require_role` callsites yet; the role is wired into authn so existing admin tooling can issue installer API keys. Higher-privilege site/zone-write paths follow in Sprint 38 when the Bridge/Gateway split lands. `src/tagpulse/models/user_schemas.py`.
- **`AssetCreate` / `AssetUpdate` external_ref validator (gap 2.8).** Rejects any of the URL-unsafe characters `. : / ? # \ [ ] @ , | & ! = $ ' * + ; %` (forbidden-character list pulled verbatim from the schema/API audit row 2.8). Empty / whitespace-only values normalise to `None`. Pydantic field validator; surfaces as 422 from the existing assets endpoints. 66 unit tests in `tests/unit/test_categories.py` covering all four `category_type` values, immutability of `category_type` on `CategoryUpdate`, `required_tags >= 1`, name/UPC length caps, the full per-character forbidden-char matrix for `external_ref`, and the four-role acceptance set for `UserCreate` / `UserUpdate`. The schema uses TagPulse's `tag` terminology throughout (see `docs/data-models.md` Â§"Where is the tag?").

Validation is format-only at the API: HTTPS-only logo URL, â‰¤2048-char URL, â‰¤255-char display name, `^#[0-9A-Fa-f]{6}$` brand colour. - `docs/adr/019-categories.md` â€” Categories as a first-class entity (status: proposed; ratification target Sprint 34). Unblocks ADR 021 scoping and the `categoryId` field in the outbound event envelope.

- `docs/adr/021-configurable-sensing-events.md` â€” **revised to v2** during sprint-33 review. v1 proposed a parallel `sensing_event_configs` table; v2 extends `rules` (8 nullable columns + new `sensing.<event_type>.<trigger>` condition types) after recognising ~60% overlap with the existing `rules`/`alerts` surface. - `docs/adr/024-position-estimation.md` â€” indoor position estimation via multi-reader RSSI triangulation in grid-style sites (status: proposed; ratification target Sprint 40). Surfaced post-audit by SME review of football-field-size deployments. Extends ADR 021 v2's `processor` enum with a third value (`trilateration`), adds `devices.position_x/y/z`, `sites.coord_system JSONB`, new `asset_positions` Timescale hypertable, and a `devices/{device_id}/status` MQTT topic for periodic reader-level status. Ships one reference algorithm (`weighted_centroid_log_distance`) behind a pluggable interface plus a first-class BYO-precomputed-positions ingest path so customers running Zebra Aurora / Impinj ItemSense / Mojix / RFcode RTLS can POST resolved fixes directly. Five of seven prerequisites already in place today (`tag_reads.signal_strength`, `tag_reads.reader_antenna`, `tag_reads.sensor_data`, `tag_reads.tag_data`, reader-side `telemetry_readings subject_kind='device'`).
- `scripts/mqtt_tap.py` â€” read-only in-VNet MQTT subscriber for triage. Run via `scripts/azd-job.sh <env> mqtt_tap.py -- [flags]` to inspect raw payloads the broker is delivering (default mirrors the worker's two topic filters: `tenants/+/devices/+/+` and `tenants/+/subjects/+/+/telemetry`). Supports `--tenant-id`/`--device-id` narrowing, `--duration` and `--max-messages` exit conditions, and JSON pretty-printing by default. Strictly observational â€” no DB writes, no state mutations. Pairs with `scripts/mqtt_canary.py` (publisher) and `scripts/azd-logs.sh` (worker-log tail).
- `scripts/tag_reads_near.py` â€” read-only in-VNet `tag_reads` inspector for triage "what landed near time T?". Run via `scripts/azd-job.sh <env> tag_reads_near.py -- --at <iso-ts> [flags]`. `--at` accepts any ISO-8601 timestamp with timezone (e.g. `2026-05-17T21:49:55Z` or `2026-05-17T14:49:55-07:00`); symmetric `--window` (default 5 min) or asymmetric `--before`/`--after` in seconds; optional `--device-id`/`--tenant-id` narrowing. Emits one JSON object per row to stdout (id, device_id, tag_id, timestamp, created_at, signal_strength, reader_antenna, epc_hex, tid, sensor_data, tag_data, lat/lng/accuracy/source) plus a one-line summary to stderr (count, earliest, latest, distinct devices, antennas seen). Useful companion to `mqtt_tap.py` for confirming what made it past the subscriber + ingestion path.
- `.githooks/pre-push` â€” blocks `git push origin main` from a clone that opts in via `git config core.hooksPath .githooks`. `scripts/start-sprint.sh` now sets this automatically; existing clones can opt in with the one-liner now documented in `CONTRIBUTING.md`. Bypass: `git push --no-verify`. Workaround for GitHub Free not supporting branch protection / rulesets on private repos.
- `docs/runbooks/github-workflows.md` â€” operator-facing catalog of every workflow in `.github/workflows/` (trigger, schedule, purpose, manual-run, failure triage). Linked from `docs/runbooks/README.md`.
- `docs/guides/contributor-workflow.md` â€” developer-facing guide covering branching, the sprint model (planning unit, not a branch), multi-PR workflow, CHANGELOG conflict resolution, and the release model (current continuous-deploy + future SemVer-tag flow). Linked from `CONTRIBUTING.md`.
- `.github/workflows/dev-wake.yml` â€” scheduled Monâ€“Fri 13:00 UTC (+ `workflow_dispatch`). Starts the dev PG Flex server if `Stopped`, restarts the active api revision to drain the stale asyncpg pool, runs `make doctor ENV=dev` as a sanity check. Closes the "every morning the dev env is dead" loop. Scope: dev only.
- `.github/workflows/dev-kv-cleanup.yml` â€” scheduled nightly 00:00 UTC (+ `workflow_dispatch`). Purges all entries from the dev KV `ipRules` and resets `publicNetworkAccess=Disabled` to match the Bicep baseline. Operators who ran `azd-grant-operator-kv.sh dev --allow-my-ip` and forgot to revoke get auto-cleaned. Scope: dev only.

### Fixes

- **Sprint 36 â€” auto-deploy backend to `dev` on every successful `main` build.** Closes the gap that left Sprint 34 (`d6dec19` categories) and Sprint 35 phases A/B/C/E (labels) un-deployed for a week: the user-visible symptom was the Categories page hanging ~5 s on every navigation because `GET /categories` returned 404 (the route was on `main` but the live `tpdev-api` revision was the May 9 image), and TanStack Query's default retry chain (1 s + 2 s + 4 s) only gave up after the third 404. Until now, `deploy-azure.yml` was `workflow_dispatch` + `v*`-tag only, so backend merges only reached `dev` when an operator manually triggered the workflow â€” which had not happened since 2026â€‘05â€‘10. The fix adds a third trigger on `workflow_run` after `build-and-push` completes on `main`: this guarantees the matching `sha-<40hex>` images already exist in ACR before the verify step runs (a `push: branches: [main]` trigger would race the upstream build). The job's `if` short-circuits when `github.event.workflow_run.conclusion != 'success'` so a failed build cannot deploy. `environment` and the concurrency group both default to `dev` on the new trigger (`inputs.environment || (github.event_name == 'workflow_run' && 'dev') || 'production'`), preserving the existing `v*`-tag â†’ `production` and manual-dispatch â†’ operator-picked behaviour, and keeping the per-env concurrency lock so a dev rollout cannot cancel a production rollout. `actions/checkout@v4` pins to `${{ github.event.workflow_run.head_sha || github.sha }}` because `workflow_run` otherwise checks out the default-branch HEAD at trigger time rather than the commit that produced the image being rolled out â€” without the pin, `scripts/azd-network-check.sh` and the other in-tree helpers would drift from the deployed code. The image-tag resolver gains a matching `workflow_run` branch that emits `sha-${TRIGGER_SHA}` (the full 40-char form `build-and-push.yml` already tags via `docker/metadata-action` `type=sha,format=long`); the existing short-SHA expansion path in "Expand image tag" is untouched. No new permissions or GitHub Environment variables required â€” re-uses the `dev` environment's OIDC federated credential already in place since Sprint 22 C4. `.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml`.

- `scripts/azd-logs.sh` â€” cap `--tail` at 300 (was 1000, which `az containerapp logs show` rejects with `--tail must be between 0 and 300`, breaking `make logs ENV=<env> SERVICE=<api|worker> SINCE=<duration>`). While here, surface that `SINCE` is *approximate*: `az containerapp logs show` has no time-based filter (only `--tail N` and `--follow`), so the script now emits a one-line stderr note when `SINCE` is provided. For true time-windowed queries, use `az monitor log-analytics query` against the env's Log Analytics workspace.
- `scripts/lib/azd-common.sh` `azd()` wrapper â€” extend the upgrade-nag filter to also strip azd 1.25's "Update available:" message (was leaking into command-substituted output and corrupting `RG` / `KV_NAME` / `ACR_NAME` in `azd-doctor.sh`, causing false reds for resource group, ACR, and KV).
- `.github/workflows/dev-wake.yml` â€” extend schedule to Monâ€“Sun (`1-7`) so the dev env is also warm for weekend on-call paging.
- `.github/workflows/dev-wake.yml` â€” fix cron expression: `1-7` is out of range for the day-of-week field (valid 0â€“6) and GitHub Actions silently disabled the schedule, so no scheduled wake fired on Sat May 16 or Sun May 17. Switched to `0 13 * * *` (every day) with a comment documenting the gotcha.
- `scripts/azd-doctor.sh` â€” probe `/health/ready` instead of the non-existent `/healthz` (was a false red).
- `scripts/lib/azd-common.sh` `aca_name` â€” fall back to ACI lookup for `mqtt` (current dev shape is `tp${env}-mqtt` ACI, not a Container App) so doctor reports its real state.
- `scripts/lib/azd-common.sh` `azd_env_resolve` â€” add `acrName` and `AZURE_ACR_LOGIN_SERVER`/`acrLoginServer` (FQDN-derived) fallbacks for `ACR_NAME` so the doctor's ACR-image check works without manually setting `AZURE_CONTAINER_REGISTRY_NAME`.
- `scripts/azd-doctor.sh` â€” KV-reachable yellow now prints the exact remediation command (`azd-grant-operator-kv.sh <env> --allow-my-ip`) instead of "firewall? RBAC?".
- `scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh` â€” fix `--allow-my-ip` against vaults with `publicNetworkAccess=Disabled`. The probe parser was looking for `Client address:` in the error, but PE-only vaults return `ForbiddenByConnection` with no client address; the probe returned empty and the script bailed before applying the firewall update. Now detects `ForbiddenByConnection` and falls straight to `api.ipify.org` instead.
- `docs/runbooks/db-failover-and-restore.md` Â§A1 â€” derive PG short name from `postgresFqdn` (azd env) instead of the non-existent `POSTGRES_SERVER_NAME`, which silently produced `--name ""` and hung the `az` call.
- `docs/runbooks/db-failover-and-restore.md` Â§A3a â€” document the api-revision restart needed to drain asyncpg's stale connection pool after the Flex server returns from `Stopped`.

### Earlier in Unreleased

- **Edge sim: explicit TLS knobs in `paho_smoke_publisher.py`** ([clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py](clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py), [clients/pi/README.md](clients/pi/README.md), [clients/pi/examples/.tp_paho_edge.env.example](clients/pi/examples/.tp_paho_edge.env.example)). Sprint 28 C6 opened `tcp/8883` on the dev broker but the smoke publisher had no `tls_set()` call, so pointing `BROKER_PORT=8883` at the broker silently hung at the TLS handshake (broker drops the connection because the client is sending raw MQTT bytes into a TLS listener). Added `--tls-ca PATH` / `TLS_CA=` and `--insecure` flags; TLS is auto-enabled when `BROKER_PORT==8883`. README now has a "TLS (port 8883)" section explaining that the dev broker's self-signed CA is **not** in the system trust store and must be distributed out-of-band.

- **CI: `deploy-azure.yml` now accepts short SHA tags** ([.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml](.github/workflows/deploy-azure.yml)). `build-and-push.yml` tags ACR images with the full 40-char commit SHA (`type=sha,format=long`) but operators almost always have a 7-char short SHA in hand from `git rev-parse --short HEAD` or the GitHub UI. Passing `image_tag=sha-aeed4a4` previously failed at the verify step even though the image was sitting in ACR as `sha-aeed4a499b618e933f0caa05e524f204d9b3ce5b`. New "Expand image tag (short SHA â†’ full SHA)" step probes ACR after Azure login and resolves any `sha-<4-39 hex>` prefix to its unique long-form match (errors with the candidate list if ambiguous). Verbatim tags (full SHA, `latest`, `v*`) continue to work unchanged.

- **Fix: MQTT subscriber crashed permanently on a single malformed payload** ([src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py](src/tagpulse/ingestion/mqtt_subscriber.py), closes [#18](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/18)). One bad publish on `â€¦/tag-reads` raised a `TypeError` out of `_handle_tag_read` (either `argument after ** must be a mapping, not list` for an array body, or `got multiple values for keyword argument 'device_id'` when the body carried its own `device_id`) and killed the subscriber task. The worker container kept reporting healthy while ingest was silently dead until restart. Three fixes:
  1. `_handle_tag_read` now accepts a single object **or** an array of objects, strips any body-supplied `device_id` (topic-derived id always wins), and per-element catches both `ValueError` and `TypeError` so one bad element only drops itself.
  2. The top-level `run()` loop wraps `_handle_message` in `try/except Exception` so any unhandled crash is logged and the loop continues consuming. `CancelledError` still propagates for graceful shutdown.
  3. `_run_mqtt_subscriber` in [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py) is now a supervised reconnect loop with 1s â†’ 60s exponential backoff so a transient failure (or any future regression that escapes the per-message guard) cannot take ingest fully offline.

  Regression coverage: [tests/unit/test_mqtt_subscriber_resilience.py](tests/unit/test_mqtt_subscriber_resilience.py) â€” five tests covering JSON list payload, single dict containing `device_id` (with assertion that topic-derived id wins), garbage bytes, JSON scalar, and a `run()`-loop test that verifies a handler `RuntimeError` doesn't stop subsequent messages from being consumed.
- **Docs: corrected MQTT `tag-reads` payload shape** ([docs/guides/device-developer-guide.md](docs/guides/device-developer-guide.md), [docs/design/edge-device-contract.md](docs/design/edge-device-contract.md), closes [#19](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/19)). The onboarding guide showed the HTTP `/tag-reads/batch` shape (`[{"device_id": â€¦, â€¦}]`) for the MQTT topic; literally following the docs triggered the [#18](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/18) crash. Now documents the canonical single-object shape (no `device_id` â€” derived from the topic), notes that the array form is also accepted, and adds an explicit "tag-read payload shape (MQTT)" subsection to the edge-device-contract spec.
- **Docs: deployment topology section in [README.md](README.md)** â€” new "Deployment topology (CI/CD vs local azd)" table clarifying that `build-and-push.yml` is registry-only, `deploy-azure.yml` is the canonical CI path that creates ACA revisions, and local `azd deploy` produces the distinctive `<app>--azd-<unix_ts>` revision suffix. Closes the documentation ask in [issue #17](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse/issues/17). Audit confirmed `build-and-push.yml` does not deploy â€” the 2026-05-09 07:49 UTC `tpdev-api--azd-1778312957` revision was a concurrent local `azd deploy`, not the workflow.
- **Docs: domain concepts 101 guide** ([docs/guides/domain-concepts-101.md](docs/guides/domain-concepts-101.md)). New plain-English primer for newcomers covering the seven primitives (Device, Tag, Asset, Product, Lot, Stock Item, Binding), why bindings have three kinds (`epc` / `tid` / `device`), where location lives (on the device, derived for everything else), the asset-tracking model (flat: asset â†” point-in-time `asset_tag_bindings`), the inventory-tracking model (3-level: product â†’ lot â†’ stock_item with inline binding columns), and an end-to-end workflow comparison table mapping each step to its API call **and** UI screen. Cross-linked from [docs/data-models.md](docs/data-models.md).
- **Edge sim: `drive_track.sh` learns `TAG_ID=...`** ([clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh](clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh)). When `TAG_ID` is set, each waypoint is published as a `tag-reads` message (with the lat/lon embedded under `location`) instead of a `/location` device-GPS update. This is what `asset_current_location`, the Data Explorer, and the Asset Path tab actually consume â€” pure `/location` messages only update `devices.last_lat/lon` and don't appear in those views. Without `TAG_ID`, behaviour is unchanged.
- **Fix: `GET /assets/{id}/path` returned 500** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/asset_location.py)). The merged-path SQL referenced `tr.reader_id`, which is not a column on `tag_reads` (the actual column is `tr.device_id`, as already used by the `asset_current_location` view in migration 024). Every call surfaced as `UndefinedColumnError: column tr.reader_id does not exist` and broke the **Assets â†’ Path** tab in the admin UI for any asset with an active binding. Fixed by switching to `tr.device_id`. Added a unit-level regression assertion against `_PATH_SQL` in [tests/unit/test_asset_location.py](tests/unit/test_asset_location.py); the bug originally slipped through because every existing path test stubbed the repository.
- **Edge smoke publisher â€” movement simulation** ([clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py](clients/pi/examples/paho_smoke_publisher.py)). Added `--track PATH`, `--track-loop`, and `--track-interp HZ` for replaying a CSV waypoint file (`lat,lon[,accuracy,dwell_s]`) over a single MQTT session, with optional linear interpolation between sparse waypoints to produce smooth high-rate GPS streams. Sample track at [clients/pi/examples/tracks/boston-loop.csv](clients/pi/examples/tracks/boston-loop.csv). For shell-driven low-rate playback (one MQTT connect per point), added [clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh](clients/pi/examples/drive_track.sh). Documented in [clients/pi/README.md](clients/pi/README.md) under "Simulating device movement".
- **Inventory simulator revamp â€” `scripts/simulate_inventory.py`** ([scripts/simulate_inventory.py](scripts/simulate_inventory.py)). Replaced the 3-SKU / shared-`LOT-A` / one-shot-reads scenario with a practical "Boston DC" warehouse: 1 site, 4 reader-bound zones (Receiving Dock / Cold Storage / Pick Floor / Shipping Dock) each with their own anchor reader, 4 distinct products with **distinct lot codes per product** (`VAX-2604-A`, `MILK-0501` near-expiry, `YOG-0428-B`, `CHS-0301-K`), and a finite pool of stock units with **stable SGTIN-96 serials** so re-runs update existing `stock_items` instead of inflating thousands of one-shot rows. Each unit follows a randomised per-unit timeline (Receiving â†’ Cold Storage â†’ Pick Floor â†’ Shipping; ~30% stop in Cold, ~20% reach Pick, ~50% ship out), generating real `subject.zone_changed` events and ENTER/TRANSFER/EXIT rows in `stock_movements`. Reads are sent at the zone-bound reader for the unit's current stage so per-zone counts on **Stock Levels** reflect actual movement. Idempotent: re-running reuses the existing site / zones / devices / products / lots / mapping / stock items. New flags: `--units` (scale pool), `--tick`, `--seed`, `--duration` (replaces old `--devices` / `--interval`). [docs/quickstart.md Â§6c](docs/quickstart.md) rewritten with the new scenario; new [docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md Â§3b](docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md) example for running it via `scripts/azd-job.sh` against a deployed env (no `--api-key` needed; KV-injected).

### Fixed

- **`azd` shell wrapper silently swallowed command failures, breaking `make doctor`.** Two related defects in [`scripts/lib/azd-common.sh`](scripts/lib/azd-common.sh) + [`scripts/azd-doctor.sh`](scripts/azd-doctor.sh) caused `make doctor ENV=dev` to exit `2` with no error message even when the underlying `azd env select dev` had failed. (1) The `azd()` wrapper captured the exit status with `if ! out=$(command azd "$@" 2>&1); then local rc=$?; â€¦`. Inside the body of an `if ! cmd; then` branch bash's `$?` is the *inverted* status â€” always `0`, because the shell only enters that branch on non-zero â€” so `rc` was silently `0` and every failed `azd` call was reported as success. Rewritten to `out=$(...); rc=$?; if (( rc != 0 )); then ...; fi`. (2) The trailing `[[ -n "$out" ]] && printf '%s\n' "$out"` made the function's exit status equal to the string-non-empty test, so a successful no-output call (e.g. newer `azd env select` versions) returned `1`. Replaced with an explicit `if` block and a final `return 0`. (3) `scripts/azd-doctor.sh` invoked `azd_env_resolve "$ENV_NAME" 2>/dev/null` to silence noise, but that helper calls `die()` on failure (which exits the whole script rather than returning), so the `else` branch printing a red status line was unreachable and operators got only `make: *** [Makefile:NN: doctor] Error 2`. Stderr is no longer redirected â€” the underlying error message now reaches the operator. Inline comments in both files document the trap so the obvious-looking refactor (collapsing back to `if !` or to `&&`) doesn't get reapplied. Pure shell change, no tests added (no shell test harness in this repo).

### Ops â€” `azd-job.sh` log-streaming fix (kills the `azd-kv-get.sh` flake)

- **Symptom.** `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev <secret>` (and any `azd-job.sh`-based wrapper) routinely returned `error: could not extract output from job log` for short-lived scripts (`get_kv_secret.py`, ~2s wall-clock). The wrapper waited 20 s then issued exactly **one** Log Analytics query â€” but Container Apps â†’ Log Analytics ingestion lag is highly variable in centralus (typically 60â€“120 s, sometimes >2 min), so the query landed before the row was indexed and returned empty. Operators had to re-run with `--update-only` after a manual `sleep 90`. Made `azd-kv-get.sh` effectively unusable for interactive secret retrieval.
- **Fix â€” two-tier log fetch in [scripts/azd-job.sh](scripts/azd-job.sh).**
  1. **Wait for terminal status first** (5 s poll instead of 10 s) so we don't race a still-running container.
  2. **Try the Container Apps data-plane log endpoint first** â€” `az containerapp job logs show --execution <name> --container tools --format text --tail 300 --only-show-errors`. This hits the live-logs API on the ACA env and bypasses Log Analytics entirely; ~instant when it works. Strip the `<RFC3339> <stream> F ` prefix the data-plane format adds so callers get bare log lines (matters for `azd-kv-get.sh`, which greps between sentinels and pipes the value to `export FOO=$(â€¦)`).
  3. **Fall back to Log Analytics with retry** â€” 12Ã— 20 s poll (4-min cap) when the data-plane returns nothing (e.g. replica already garbage-collected on `--update-only`). Eliminates the single-shot race.
  - Net: `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev --list` and `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev <name>` now return clean output in <30 s for the live path, with a graceful fallback for stale executions.
- **`scripts/azd-kv-get.sh` â€” strip the wrapper's 4-space indent inside the sentinel block** ([scripts/azd-kv-get.sh](scripts/azd-kv-get.sh)) so `printf '%s\n' "$(echo "$PAYLOAD" | tail -1)"` returns the raw secret value, not `    <value>` with leading whitespace. Header comment updated to reflect the data-plane-first strategy.
- **End-to-end validated** against `tpdev`: `--list` returns the 6 KV secrets in <20 s; single-secret retrieval (`mqtt-broker-password`, 32-byte value) round-trips cleanly into a shell variable.
- **Backlog (Sprint 24+).** "Production-grade Bastion + jumpbox standard for staging + production envs" already on the [Sprint 23 deferred list](docs/roadmap.md#deferred-to-sprint-24) covers the structural alternative â€” laptop direct-to-KV access via a VNet-resident jumpbox â€” for operators who prefer Azure Portal "Show Secret Value" over the tools-job round-trip.

### Ops â€” In-VNet KV secret retrieval (`scripts/azd-kv-get.sh` + `scripts/get_kv_secret.py`)

- **Closes the corporate-proxy / WSL2 / Cloud Shell hole in `azd-grant-operator-kv.sh --allow-my-ip`.** The IP-allowlist path assumes a stable operator egress IP, but operators behind a corporate firewall (or running `az` from Azure Cloud Shell / an Azure VM) get a rotating SNAT IP from a Microsoft-owned pool, so each retry of `az keyvault secret show` fails with a different `ForbiddenByFirewall` client address. Allowlisting the entire pool is impractical and the network team won't hand it out.
- **[scripts/get_kv_secret.py](scripts/get_kv_secret.py).** Tiny tools-job-side script: `argparse` + `DefaultAzureCredential` + `SecretClient.get_secret(name)`. Reads `--vault` from `$TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` (which `tools-job.bicep` already wires in alongside `DATABASE_URL` etc.) and prints the value bracketed by `===KV_SECRET_BEGIN===` / `===KV_SECRET_END===` sentinels so the wrapper can grep it cleanly out of the streamed Log Analytics tail. `--list` enumerates secret names via `client.list_properties_of_secrets()` (bracketed by `===KV_SECRET_LIST_BEGIN===` / `===KV_SECRET_LIST_END===`) so operators don't have to guess.
- **[scripts/azd-kv-get.sh](scripts/azd-kv-get.sh).** Operator-facing one-liner: `export FOO=$(scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev tagpulse-test-corp-admin-key)` for retrieval, `scripts/azd-kv-get.sh dev --list` for the menu. Delegates to `scripts/azd-job.sh` with `--allow-stale` (the wrapper itself doesn't ship in the image; the script body does, as long as the image was built since this commit landed). Captures the streamed output, awks the value/names out of the sentinels, prints them to stdout. Exit-code propagation + full-log dump on failure. The script header now also documents the standard secret-name menu (Bicep-seeded `jwt-secret` / `postgres-admin-password` / `mqtt-broker-password` plus the smoke-setup `tagpulse-<tenant-slug>-{admin,editor,viewer}-key` pattern).
- **[docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md Â§3d](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) updated** â€” step 2 now leads with the tools-job route as the preferred path for Sprint 23-B-hardened envs, with the IP-allowlist fallback documented as "only if your laptop has a stable public IP", and inlines the secret-name menu + `--list` discovery command. The common-failures-table `ForbiddenByConnection` row points at both options with the corporate-proxy caveat called out.
- **No code in `src/`, no infra changes.** Reuses the existing tools-job UAMI's `Key Vault Secrets User` role and the existing `azd-job.sh` execution + log-tailing plumbing.

### Ops â€” Operator KV-access helper (`scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh`)

- **New [scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh](scripts/azd-grant-operator-kv.sh).** Closes the operator-self-service gap that bit the first `tpdev` smoke run: after `smoke_setup.py --regenerate-key` pushed the rotated admin/editor/viewer API keys to KV, retrieving them from a laptop with `az keyvault secret show` failed twice â€” once on RBAC (`ForbiddenByRbac`), then again on network ACL (`ForbiddenByConnection / Public network access is disabled`). The api/worker UAMIs and the `tpdev-tools` UAMI receive their KV roles at provision time via [identity.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/identity.bicep), but Bicep deliberately doesn't pin a human principal so the same template works for any operator. The script handles both gaps in one call:
  - **RBAC mode (default)** â€” assigns "Key Vault Secrets User" (read-only) to the signed-in identity at the deployment KV scope. Idempotent; skips if the assignment already exists. Use `--role "Key Vault Secrets Officer"` for write access, `--principal <oid>` to grant a different principal (e.g. a CI service principal).
  - **Network-ACL mode (`--allow-my-ip` / `--revoke-my-ip`)** â€” flips `publicNetworkAccess` from `Disabled` (Sprint 23-B hardening default) to `Enabled` with `defaultAction=Deny` + the operator's current public IP added to `ipRules`. Net effect: private-endpoint traffic AND your one IP reach the data plane; everything else stays blocked. The corresponding `--revoke-my-ip` flips it back to fully private. Pairs with `--allow-my-ip` running RBAC in the same invocation so a fresh operator gets both in one shot.
- **Documented in [docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md Â§3d](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md).** Step 2 of the seed-demo-tenant flow now points at the script with both branches called out (open-network vs Sprint 23-B-hardened envs).

### Docs â€” Edge primer staleness audit

- **[docs/refs/edge-hardware-and-rfid-primer.md](docs/refs/edge-hardware-and-rfid-primer.md) â€” refresh "Still to land" list.** The primer claimed Sprint 14 telemetry/location wiring + `epc`/`tid`/`tag_data` fields, Sprint 16 token-revoke handling + conformance harness, and Sprint 17b client-side mTLS were all outstanding â€” every one of those landed in its named sprint. Replaced with a "Shipped since" block (with file links) and a tighter "Still open" list capturing the genuine remaining gaps: no `MqttTransport.update_token()` hot-swap, conformance harness doesn't yet exercise telemetry/location/token-revoke, and Sprint 17c broker-side mTLS rollout is still planned.

### Ops â€” `azd-job.sh` env-wipe fix + smoke_setup connection robustness + tools-job AZURE_CLIENT_ID

- **`scripts/azd-job.sh` â€” preserve env on container PATCH** ([scripts/azd-job.sh](scripts/azd-job.sh)). The wrapper sends an ARM PATCH to `properties.template.containers[0]` to override the container's `command` + `args` at start time. ARM PATCH replaces the container object wholesale (matched by `name`), so the previous body â€” which only set `name`/`image`/`command`/`args` â€” silently wiped every Bicep-declared env var on the tools-job (`DATABASE_URL`, `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL`, `TAGPULSE_API_URL`, `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME`, the lot). Symptom: `scripts/azd-job.sh dev smoke_setup.py â€¦` hit `[Errno 111] Connect call failed ('127.0.0.1', 5432)` because `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` wasn't there to override the local-dev default. PATCH body now round-trips the existing `env` + `resources` arrays via `jq`.
- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py` â€” connect via component env vars when present** ([scripts/smoke_setup.py](scripts/smoke_setup.py)). Even with `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` restored, asyncpg's DSN parser blew up on the Flex Server admin password (`ValueError: invalid literal for int() with base 10: 's6oETxfj3tY9WL'`) because the Bicep-generated password contains URL-special characters. New `_connect_db()` helper prefers `POSTGRES_HOST` / `POSTGRES_USER` / `POSTGRES_PASSWORD` / `POSTGRES_DB` (already wired by [tools-job.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep)) as kwargs to `asyncpg.connect(..., ssl="require")`, falling back to `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` for local dev. Sidesteps DSN-encoding entirely.
- **`tools-job.bicep` â€” wire `AZURE_CLIENT_ID` so `DefaultAzureCredential` resolves the UAMI** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). After (1) and (2) above, `smoke_setup --regenerate-key` got all the way to the Key Vault push step and then died with `ManagedIdentityCredential: '(invalid_scope) 400, Unable to load the proper Managed Identity'`. The UAMI was attached, but the `azure-identity` SDK's managed-identity probe couldn't pick *which* identity to use. Fix: surface `identity.outputs.clientId` as a new `userAssignedIdentityClientId` param on the tools-job module and set it as `AZURE_CLIENT_ID` env var on the container. The api/worker are unaffected because they reach KV via ACA's `secretRef`-with-`identity` path (different code path) rather than the SDK.
- **End-to-end validated.** `scripts/azd-job.sh dev smoke_setup.py -- --full --with-roles --with-subject-telemetry --regenerate-key` now succeeds against `tpdev` â€” provisions tenant + admin/editor/viewer users with KV-pushed keys, site + geofence zones, telemetry model, rules, Sprint 19 opt-in, Sprint 21 cutover probe.

### Docs â€” Deployment paths

- **[docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) â€” new "Deployment paths" section.** Documents the three distinct flows that put TagPulse on Azure (CI `build-and-push.yml` on push to `main`, `deploy-azure.yml` on `v*` tag / manual dispatch, and operator `azd up` / `azd deploy`) with a comparison table showing which flow builds images, which updates Azure, and which invokes the `azd` predeploy/postdeploy hooks. Captures the recurring confusion that follow-up PRs touching `scripts/azd-*.sh` (e.g. PR #15) do not auto-deploy â€” those hooks only run in the local operator flow.

### Ops â€” `azd up` hook fixes (follow-up to PR #14)

- **`scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh` â€” fix `get_azd` helper** ([scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh](scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh)). The previous shape (`azd env get-value KEY 2>/dev/null | tr -d '\r'`) silently captured `azd`'s "key not found" error text as the value, because `azd env get-value` writes that error to **STDOUT** (not stderr) and the caller only checked emptiness. The pg-ensure script's predeploy hook then tried to query `az postgres flexible-server show -n "$PG_FQDN%%.*"` with the multiline error string and exited 1 on every `azd up`. Helper now gates on the subprocess exit code (matches the working pattern already used in `azure.yaml`'s postprovision hook). Also adds a fallback to the canonical Bicep output name `postgresFqdn` when `AZURE_POSTGRES_FQDN` (an alias only set by `azd-network-check.sh` callers) is unset.
- **`scripts/azd-network-check.sh` â€” extract IP + soft-fail on ACA exec throttle** ([scripts/azd-network-check.sh](scripts/azd-network-check.sh)). Two changes: (1) `az containerapp exec` now prefixes its stdout with `INFO: Connecting to the container '<name>'...` (CLI 2.65+); the previous `tail -1` captured that line as the resolved IP, breaking the `^10\.10\.` regex assertion â€” replaced with `grep -Eo '([0-9]{1,3}\.){3}[0-9]{1,3}' | tail -1`. (2) The ACA exec websocket is aggressively rate-limited (HTTP 429) on back-to-back `azd deploy` runs, and a hard fail there blocked every subsequent deploy until the throttle cleared. Inside-VNet resolution failures are now WARN by default (one quick retry then continue); set `AZURE_NETWORK_CHECK_STRICT=true` to restore the hard fail on first VNet rollouts or CI smokes. The outside-VNet block check (KV public REST â†’ 403) still runs unconditionally.

### Ops â€” Postgres auto-stop self-heal

- **New [scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh](scripts/azd-pg-ensure-running.sh).** Idempotent: no-op when the Flexible Server is `Ready`, starts it (and polls up to ~5 min) when `Stopped`. Triggered by a real outage on `tpdev`: Burstable-tier (B1ms) Flex servers auto-stop after 7 days of inactivity, which silently 5xx's the entire backend â€” the api replica keeps running but every DB call fails (`asyncpg.exceptions.ConnectionDoesNotExistError` â†’ `TimeoutError on asyncpg.connect`), `/health/ready` flips unhealthy, and ACA stops routing ingress traffic. Reads `AZURE_RESOURCE_GROUP` + `AZURE_POSTGRES_FQDN` from `azd env` (or plain env vars), derives the server name from the FQDN's first label.
- **Wired as `predeploy` hook in [azure.yaml](azure.yaml).** Ensures `azd deploy` self-heals before pushing new images, so the postdeploy migrations-job poll doesn't hang against a dead DB.
- **Runbook entry** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) common-failures table). Documents the `Stopped`-server failure mode (the symptom is "backend completely down" â€” easy to misdiagnose as ACA, networking, or app-level) plus the manual recovery: start the server, then `az containerapp revision restart` to drain the stale asyncpg connection pool.

PR #11's tools-job set `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` and granted `Key Vault Secrets Officer` to the workload UAMI on the assumption the script honored it; PR #12's runbook step "pull the rotated key from Key Vault" was therefore broken. Cherry-picked the D3 commit (script changes + `[azure]` extra deps in [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml)) so the tools-job, the role assignment, and the runbook all line up with real code paths. ([scripts/smoke_setup.py](scripts/smoke_setup.py))
- **Runbook fix: `azd env get-value uiFqdn` â†’ `staticWebAppHostname`** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md) Â§3d step 4). `uiFqdn` is not an `azd` env output; the SPA hostname is exposed as `staticWebAppHostname` (matches Â§3a + Â§3b earlier in the same runbook). The drill would have failed at the manual-verification step.

### Sprint 26 â€” Tools-job validation (D1 + D2)

- **D1 â€” Post-deploy seed-tenant smoke section** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). New `### 3d â€” Seed the demo tenant + verify Tenant ID login` subsection between Phase 3c (operational scripts contract) and Phase 4 (CI/CD). Four-step drill: `scripts/azd-job.sh dev smoke_setup.py -- --full --with-roles --with-subject-telemetry --regenerate-key`, pull the freshly rotated admin key from Key Vault (job's `--key-vault-name` default keeps plaintext out of Log Analytics), curl `GET /tenant/config` to confirm the api sees `Test Corp`, then verify the SPA Tenant ID login flow lands on the dashboard. Closes the Sprint 25 follow-up where the deployed SPA had no working tenant out of the box. Includes a fallback diagnostic (`az containerapp job execution list`) for the two known failure modes (KV Secrets Officer not yet propagated, tools-job in the wrong VNet).
- **D2 â€” CI smoke that the api image still imports `scripts/`** ([.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml](.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml)). New `Smoke â€” tools image imports scripts/` step, gated on `matrix.component == 'api'`, runs `docker run --entrypoint python <imageid> -c "import scripts.smoke_setup, scripts.simulate_devices, scripts.simulate_assets, scripts.simulate_inventory, scripts.benchmark_pg_metrics"`. Catches the failure mode where someone moves a script under a subdirectory or renames a module without updating the tools-job runbook. Required `load: true` on the `docker/build-push-action` step so the just-built image is available in the local daemon for the smoke (coexists with `push: true` on non-PR builds).

### Sprint 26 â€” Tools-job + wrapper (B1 + B2 + C1 + C2)

- **B1 â€” New module [`deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep`](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/tools-job.bicep).** Container Apps Job (manual trigger, `replicaTimeout: 1800` so `smoke_setup --full` + a slow simulator warm-up fit, `replicaRetryLimit: 0` since operational scripts aren't migration-style idempotent). Reuses the api image (Sprint 26 A1 baked `scripts/` into it) and the workload UAMI (so KV / ACR / Postgres access "just works"). Default command is a no-op import smoke (`python -c "import scripts.smoke_setup"`); `scripts/azd-job.sh` overrides command + args at start time. Env wiring matches `migrations-job.bicep` for `POSTGRES_*` + `DATABASE_URL`, plus three sprint-26 additions: `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_DB_URL` (raw asyncpg URL for `smoke_setup.py`), `TAGPULSE_API_URL` (in-cluster api FQDN), and `TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` (so the D3 KV-push code path is the default inside the job â€” plaintext keys never hit Log Analytics).
- **B1 ride-along â€” Key Vault Secrets Officer on the workload UAMI** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/identity.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/identity.bicep)). New role assignment so the tools-job can *write* secrets to KV (not just read them). Grant is on the same UAMI used by api/worker/migrations â€” slightly broader than strictly needed but avoids fragmenting the identity model. The api/worker code paths never call `set_secret`, so in practice only the tools-job exercises the role. Closes the D3 follow-up the previous PR called out.
- **B2 â€” Wired `toolsJob` into [`workload.bicep`](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep) + outputs** ([deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep)). New module call (depends on `apiApp` for the FQDN, `kv` for the vault name, `postgres` for secrets). New `toolsJobName` output so `scripts/azd-job.sh` resolves the job from `azd env get-values` instead of hard-coding. Image points at `tagpulse-api:${imageTag}` â€” same tag as the api/worker, so `azd deploy api` keeps the tools-job in lock-step with the api's bundled `scripts/`. `az bicep build deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep` clean.
- **C1 â€” `scripts/azd-job.sh <env> <script> [-- <script argsâ€¦>]`** ([scripts/azd-job.sh](scripts/azd-job.sh)). Resolves `toolsJobName` + RG from `azd env get-values`, patches the job's container `command` + `args` via `az rest` (the `containerapp job update` CLI doesn't expose them yet â€” preview gap), starts the execution, polls `properties.status` with a 30-min timeout, then tails Log Analytics filtered by `ContainerJobName_s` + `ExecutionName_s`. Distinct exit codes for usage (1), azd/auth failure (2), timeout (3), and non-`Succeeded` terminal status (4). `--update-only` skips the start and re-tails the most recent execution â€” recovers from terminal disconnect mid-run. Refuses to run with a dirty working tree or unpushed commits unless `--allow-stale` is passed (the job runs the *deployed* image, so local script edits are silently invisible until the next `azd deploy`).
- **C2 â€” New runbook [docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md](docs/runbooks/operational-tooling.md).** Four worked examples (seed the demo tenant, rotate the demo admin key, push fake telemetry for a load smoke, re-tail after disconnect), an explicit "what NOT to run via the job" table (`load_test.py`, the workflow scripts, future destructive scripts), the stale-image gotcha, and a troubleshooting matrix covering the LA ingestion lag, the `Forbidden` case if the D3 role assignment didn't take, and the `ImportError: scripts.smoke_setup` case (image pre-dates A1).
