### Sprint 26 â€” D3 (early): Key Vault push for `smoke_setup.py`

- **`scripts/smoke_setup.py --key-vault-name <vault>`** ([scripts/smoke_setup.py](scripts/smoke_setup.py), [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml), [docs/roadmap.md](docs/roadmap.md)). Promoted from "Sprint 27+ deferred" into Phase D3 because the Sprint 26 tools-job's stdout will land in Log Analytics with 90-day retention â€” printing plaintext keys there would create a leak path the runbook can't honestly recommend against. When the flag is set (or `$TAGPULSE_SMOKE_KEY_VAULT_NAME` is exported), each freshly issued admin/role API key is pushed to KV as `tagpulse-<tenant-slug>-<role>-key` via `azure-keyvault-secrets` + `DefaultAzureCredential` (lazy-imported so pure-local dev keeps working without the optional `azure` extra installed). The script's stdout shows only vault + secret name + version; the end-of-run `export TAGPULSE_API_KEY=â€¦` line becomes `export TAGPULSE_API_KEY=$(az keyvault secret show --vault-name <vault> --name <secret> --query value -o tsv)` so an operator with `Key Vault Secrets User` can still pick the key up. `azure-identity>=1.19` + `azure-keyvault-secrets>=4.9` added to the existing `[azure]` optional-extra; the api image will pick them up when Sprint 26 A1 lands the `COPY scripts/` line. Bicep follow-up (the tools-job's MI getting `Key Vault Secrets Officer` on the env's vault) lands with B1 â€” until then the flag works from a developer laptop with `az login`.

### Sprint 25 â€” Hotfix: SWA CORS plumbing

- **`corsOriginsExtra` parameter wired through Bicep** ([deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam](deploy/azure/bicep/main.bicepparam), [deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep)). Sprint 24 A2 surfaced `Settings.cors_origins` in `/health/ready` but never passed an env var to the api Container App, so every cloud deploy ran with the dev default `http://localhost:5173` and the SPA's fetches got blocked by the browser. `workload.bicep` now feeds `'${corsOriginsExtra},https://${ui.outputs.defaultHostname}'` into the api module so the SWA hostname is auto-appended at provision time. The SWA module's `apiUrl` setting is no longer wired from `apiApp.outputs.fqdn` (would create a module cycle now that the api references the SWA hostname); the UI repo bakes `VITE_API_BASE_URL` at build time from `vars.VITE_API_BASE_URL` so the runtime app-setting was cosmetic anyway. Verified live against `tagpulse-dev-rg`: `/health/ready` reports both origins in `config.cors.allow_origins`.
- **SWA `azd-service-name=ui` tag** ([deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/workload.bicep)). The Phase D rotation cron filters `az staticwebapp list --query "[?tags.\"azd-service-name\"=='ui']"`; without the tag the lookup returned empty and the cron would silently no-op. Adds the standard `azd-service-name` tag the api / worker / migrations modules already use.

### Sprint 25 â€” Frontend Resilience & Observability (Phase A â€” backend health & CSP support)

> [docs/roadmap.md Â§ Sprint 25](docs/roadmap.md). Phase A unblocks the UI repo's remaining slices: B5 (CSP report-only header in `staticwebapp.config.json`) needs A3 to ship first, and B3/B4 (deploy-time + post-deploy smokes) need a healthy api with the new `/health/live` contract.

- **A1 â€” `/health/live` SPA-polling contract** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py), [Dockerfile](Dockerfile), [.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml](.github/workflows/build-and-push.yml)). Body shape switches from the legacy `{"status":"ok"}` to `{"status":"alive","version":"<git-sha>","build_time":"<iso8601>"}`; `Cache-Control: no-store` is set on the response so the SWA edge / browser back-cache never memoize a stale "alive" (which would silently defeat the SPA's startup gate when the api goes down). Build identity is baked at image build time via the new `BUILD_VERSION` + `BUILD_TIME` Docker build-args; the GHA matrix populates them with `${{github.sha}}` and a UTC ISO-8601 timestamp computed once per job. Local `docker build` without `--build-arg` keeps the dev sentinels (`dev` / `unknown`). `/health` (no path suffix) is unchanged for k8s probes that pre-date `/live`.
- **A2 â€” CORS preflight max-age** ([src/tagpulse/core/config.py](src/tagpulse/core/config.py), [src/tagpulse/api/main.py](src/tagpulse/api/main.py)). New `Settings.cors_preflight_max_age_seconds` (default 0; the strict-mode validator forces 600 in non-dev when left at 0, and explicit non-zero values from `CORS_PREFLIGHT_MAX_AGE_SECONDS` survive untouched). Wired into `CORSMiddleware`'s `max_age=`. Cuts 60â€“80ms off the first-paint-to-login-button latency on cold tabs by letting the browser cache the OPTIONS preflight result.
- **A3 â€” `POST /security/csp-report` endpoint** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/security.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/security.py)). Accepts both browser report shapes: the Chromium/Safari legacy `application/csp-report` envelope (`{"csp-report": {...}}`) and the Reporting API `application/reports+json` array of `{type, body}` envelopes. Emits a structured WARN log with `(client_ip, blocked_uri, document_uri, violated_directive, source_file, line_number, column_number, user_agent)` and increments the Prometheus counter `tagpulse_csp_violations_total{directive=...}`. Per-IP sliding-window rate limit at 10 reports / 60s â€” same in-process trade-off as the Sprint 22 A4 limiter; a multi-replica api may admit up to 10Â·N reports/min cluster-wide, which is fine for this endpoint. Open without auth (browsers don't send credentials on report POSTs by design); `/security/csp-report` is added to the tenant-keyed limiter's bypass list. Returns `204` on success, `429` when capped, and `204` (logged + dropped) on malformed JSON so a misbehaving extension cannot 500 the api.
- **A4 â€” Runbook update** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). `/health/live` smoke now asserts the new `{status, version, build_time}` shape + `Cache-Control: no-store`. New **Â§3b â€” SPA-vs-api consistency smoke** pulls `index.html` from the SWA, asserts `/health/ready` against the embedded api URL, and verifies the SWA hostname is in `config.cors.allow_origins` â€” catches the most insidious post-deploy failure (SPA built against a stale `VITE_API_BASE_URL`). New **Â§3c â€” CSP violation triage** documents the report shape, the Log Analytics KQL for top violations, and the triage priority order (`script-src` / `connect-src` are policy actually breaking the SPA; `img-src` / `font-src` are typically third-party extension noise).
- **Tests** â€” 13 new unit tests in [tests/unit/test_sprint25_phase_a.py](tests/unit/test_sprint25_phase_a.py) cover the `/health/live` contract (body shape, `Cache-Control: no-store`, latency budget, legacy `/health` unchanged), the CORS max-age policy in dev / non-dev / explicit-override paths, and the CSP-report endpoint across both report shapes, the per-IP rate limit, the no-auth contract, and the malformed-JSON path. `make check` clean (516 unit tests + 1 skipped, ruff + mypy green).

### Sprint 25 â€” Frontend Resilience & Observability (Phase D â€” operational + Phase E â€” multi-cloud follow-up)

> [docs/roadmap.md Â§ Sprint 25](docs/roadmap.md). Phase D automates the SWA deployment-token rotation that Sprint 24 A1 wired by hand; Phase E promotes the Sprint 24 D3 portable-UI stub into executable recipes paired with a cross-cloud DR-drill walkthrough.

- **D1 â€” `scripts/azd-ui-token-rotate.sh <env>`** ([scripts/azd-ui-token-rotate.sh](scripts/azd-ui-token-rotate.sh)). Runs `az staticwebapp secrets reset-api-key`, re-reads the new value, and writes it into the `9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI` repo's `<env>` GitHub Environment secret via `gh secret set --body -` so the token never touches a temp file. Prints the new token's last-4-chars for operator audit; the full token is written via the `gh` pipe and then dropped. Built-in 60-day idempotency gate (parses the JSONL audit log) refuses to rotate twice in quick succession unless `--force` is passed â€” the safety net against a manual rotation racing the cron. Mirrors the Sprint 24 A1 script's bash conventions (`set -euo pipefail`, `az`/`azd`/`gh`/`jq` preflight, `azd env get-value` capture). Audit log lives in `deploy/azure/.audit/ui-token-rotation.jsonl` (gitignored â€” local trail only; the GHA cron in D2 keeps the canonical record in run logs). Distinct exit codes for usage / pre-rotation auth failure (1), post-rotation `gh` failure (2 â€” operator must complete manually), and idempotency-gate refusal (3).
- **D2 â€” `.github/workflows/rotate-ui-token.yml`** ([.github/workflows/rotate-ui-token.yml](.github/workflows/rotate-ui-token.yml)). Quarterly cron (`'0 9 1 1,4,7,10 *'` â€” 09:00 UTC on the 1st of Jan/Apr/Jul/Oct) plus `workflow_dispatch` with optional comma-separated env-list and `force: bool` inputs. Matrix runs D1 against `dev` / `staging` / `production`, each leg gated by the env-list input so a manual run can target a single env. OIDC-federated `azure/login@v2` per Environment using the `AZURE_CLIENT_ID` / `AZURE_TENANT_ID` / `AZURE_SUBSCRIPTION_ID` variables already wired by `scripts/azd-cicd-setup.sh` (Sprint 22 C4); the cron job re-hydrates the azd env from the live RG (looks up the SWA by `azd-service-name=ui` tag) instead of relying on persisted state. Cross-repo `gh secret set` uses a fine-scoped repo-only PAT (`UI_REPO_SECRETS_PAT`) â€” rotate it alongside the SWA tokens; the audit log captures last-4-chars on every run. On any matrix-leg failure, opens a GitHub issue tagged `ops` + `security` with the run URL and a manual-recovery one-liner.
- **E1 â€” `deploy/portable/ui/` executable recipes** ([deploy/portable/ui/README.md](deploy/portable/ui/README.md)). Promoted the Sprint 24 D3 structure-only stub into three concrete provider blocks: AWS S3 + CloudFront with the two-pass cache-headers split (hashed assets `public, max-age=31536000, immutable`; `index.html` `no-store, must-revalidate`) followed by a targeted CloudFront invalidation on `/index.html` only; Cloudflare Pages via `wrangler pages deploy ./dist --project-name=tagpulse-ui` (Cloudflare auto-provisions the project on first deploy and handles the cache-headers split itself); and GCP Cloud Storage + Cloud LB using the same two-pass pattern. New **Cross-cloud DR drill** section paired with the Sprint 22 D-3 backend DR runbook documents the full UI-failover path: fetch the `dist.zip` artifact from the UI repo's GHA build, rebuild against a backup-backend FQDN if the api hostname differs (`VITE_API_BASE_URL` is build-time-bound), run the upload recipe, and CNAME the user-facing custom domain to the backup CDN with a pre-staged TTL=60 record. Per-provider drill notes call out IAM scope (AWS), atomic-deploy semantics (Cloudflare), and edge-invalidation propagation lag (GCP). Real Bicep / Terraform for the AWS path is still deferred Sprint 26+ (gated on a real customer asking for AWS hosting).

### Hotfix â€” Azure MQTT broker reachability (`/health/ready` 503)

- **Emit `MQTT_BROKER_HOST` + `MQTT_BROKER_PORT` from Bicep** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep)). Pydantic `Settings` reads `MQTT_BROKER_HOST` / `MQTT_BROKER_PORT`, **not** `MQTT_BROKER_URL`; the Bicep contract was URL-only, so on Azure both the `/health/ready` TCP probe and the worker subscriber fell back to the Settings defaults (`localhost:1883`) and the readiness check stayed 503 with `mqtt: down (Connection refused)` even though the broker container was reachable from the Container Apps subnet. The module now derives `brokerHost` / `brokerPort` by stripping `mqtt://` / `mqtts://` from `mqttBrokerUrl` and injects both env vars into the api + worker container env (alongside the existing `MQTT_BROKER_URL` for forward-compat).
- **Mosquitto entrypoint chowns the generated password file** ([docker/mosquitto-entrypoint.sh](docker/mosquitto-entrypoint.sh)). When the entrypoint runs as root and writes `/mosquitto/config/mosquitto.passwd` via `mosquitto_passwd -b -c`, the file is owned by root and the unprivileged `mosquitto` user (uid 1883) cannot read it â€” broker exits with `Error: Unable to open password file ... Permission denied`. The script now `chown mosquitto:mosquitto` + `chmod 0640` the file after generation so the broker can start under its own uid.

### Hotfix â€” Azure PG Flex compatibility for TimescaleDB

- **Pin `postgresVersion` to `15`** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep)). Azure Database for PostgreSQL Flexible Server **does not** ship the TimescaleDB extension on PG16 yet; `CREATE EXTENSION timescaledb` on PG16 silently drops the connection mid-statement. The Bicep default was `'16'`, so a fresh provision produced an unusable database. Pinning to PG15 (which is fully supported) is the only reliable path until Microsoft adds PG16 support.
- **Include platform `shared_preload_libraries` defaults when adding `timescaledb`** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/postgres.bicep)). The Flex Server `shared_preload_libraries` parameter **overwrites** the platform value rather than appending; setting it to `'timescaledb'` alone removes the platform-managed `pg_cron` and `pg_stat_statements` and leaves the server in a state where `CREATE EXTENSION timescaledb` again drops the connection. Value is now `'pg_cron,pg_stat_statements,timescaledb'` and the parameter has a long-form comment explaining the overwrite-not-append behavior.
- **Migration 031 is license-aware and idempotent** ([migrations/versions/031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py](migrations/versions/031_telemetry_subject_kinds_and_caggs.py)). Azure PG Flex ships TimescaleDB in **Apache-2** edition only; continuous aggregates (`CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW â€¦ WITH (timescaledb.continuous)` + `add_continuous_aggregate_policy`) are TSL-licensed and fail with `FeatureNotSupportedError: functionality not supported under the current "apache" license`. The `tenants.telemetry_subject_kinds` column is now added with `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` so partial runs don't break re-execution; `current_setting('timescaledb.license', true) = 'apache'` short-circuits both `upgrade()` and `downgrade()` past the cagg DDL. Local Docker (TSL edition) gets caggs as before; Azure Flex skips them and the application falls through to live `time_bucket()` queries.
- **`TimescaleTelemetryReadingsRepository.aggregate()` falls back to live `time_bucket` when caggs are absent** ([src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py](src/tagpulse/repositories/timescaledb/telemetry.py)). A process-cached `pg_class` probe (`_caggs_available`) detects whether `cagg_telemetry_1m` and `cagg_telemetry_1h` exist; when they don't, both the `bucket_seconds=60` and `=3600` paths route to the same live `time_bucket(make_interval(secs => :secs), â€¦)` SQL the `else` branch already used. Apache-edition deployments serve `/telemetry/aggregates` correctly with no client-visible difference (the only cost is computing aggregates from the raw hypertable on each request).

### Hotfix â€” Azure deploy DATABASE_URL incompatible with asyncpg

- **Bicep `DATABASE_URL` switched from `?sslmode=require` to `?ssl=require`** ([deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/container-app.bicep), [deploy/azure/bicep/modules/migrations-job.bicep](deploy/azure/bicep/modules/migrations-job.bicep)). Migrations job + api + worker all use `postgresql+asyncpg://...`; asyncpg's `connect()` does not accept the libpq query parameter `sslmode`, so the migrations job crashed with `TypeError: connect() got an unexpected keyword argument 'sslmode'` and the api revision never became ready (the readiness probe stayed 503 because the schema was never applied). Symptom: `curl https://${apiFqdn}/health/live` hangs because both revisions of `tpdev-api` are `ActivationFailed` with 0/1 replicas ready. Diagnosis path: Container Apps env Log Analytics â†’ `ContainerAppConsoleLogs_CL | where ContainerName_s == 'migrations'` â†’ traceback shows the offending kwarg. Fix is a one-character change (`sslmode` â†’ `ssl`); both forms mean "TLS required" but only the latter is asyncpg-native. ARM template `deploy/azure/bicep/main.json` regenerated.

### Sprint 24 â€” Frontend cloud deployment (backend prerequisites + skeletons)

> [ADR-018](docs/adr/018-frontend-cloud-deployment.md), [docs/design/frontend-deployment.md](docs/design/frontend-deployment.md), [docs/roadmap.md Â§ Sprint 24](docs/roadmap.md). Phases A/C/D land here; Phase B (the actual SPA shipping path) ships in [9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI](https://github.com/9owlsboston/TagPulse-UI).

#### Phase A â€” Backend prerequisites

- **`scripts/azd-ui-token.sh`** ([scripts/azd-ui-token.sh](scripts/azd-ui-token.sh)). Read-only helper that prints the Static Web App `apiKey` for env `<env>` to stdout via `az staticwebapp secrets list`. Refuses to print to a TTY without `--print` to keep the deployment token out of bash history / scrollback. Reads `AZURE_STATIC_WEB_APPS_NAME` + `AZURE_RESOURCE_GROUP` from `azd env get-value` using the same stdout-error-trap `get()` helper as the other azd scripts. A1.
- **`/health/ready` surfaces `cors.allow_origins`** ([src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py](src/tagpulse/api/routes/health.py)). New `cors.allow_origins` array under the existing `config` snapshot; closes the most likely "SPA loads but every API call is blocked by CORS" failure mode by letting operators verify the SWA hostname is wired into the deployed api revision without shelling into the container. A2.
- **`static-web-app.bicep` audit pinned** ([tests/unit/test_sprint24_phase_a.py](tests/unit/test_sprint24_phase_a.py)). Test asserts no `apiKey`/`listSecrets` output and pins the exact output set (`defaultHostname`/`id`/`name`) so a future contributor can't accidentally land the SWA deployment token in `azd env get-values` or git-status traces. A3.
- **First-deploy runbook Phase 3a** ([docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md)). New step between the smoke tests and CI/CD wiring: copy `staticWebAppHostname` Bicep output into `CORS_ORIGINS` in `deploy/azure/.env.<env>`, then `azd-env-load.sh <env> && azd provision` to push the new origin list into the api revision. Order matters â€” without this, the SPA loads but every fetch is rejected by the strict-mode CORS validator. A4.

#### Phase C â€” Operator documentation

- **`docs/runbooks/ui-first-deploy.md`** ([docs/runbooks/ui-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/ui-first-deploy.md)). Six-phase checklist mirroring [azure-first-deploy.md](docs/runbooks/azure-first-deploy.md): prereqs â†’ per-env bootstrap (UI repo) â†’ first manual deploy â†’ smoke tests â†’ CI/CD wiring â†’ production cutover gates. Top-N common-failures table, decommission recipe, cross-references to the SWA Bicep + token helper. C1.
- **README cross-links** ([README.md](README.md), [deploy/azure/README.md](deploy/azure/README.md), [docs/runbooks/README.md](docs/runbooks/README.md)). Both deployment-section READMEs now link to the UI runbook alongside the backend runbook; runbooks index updated with the new entry plus the previously-undocumented `azd-survival-guide.md` and `sprint-23-network-cutover.md` rows. C2, C3.

README with provider-mapping table (Azure SWA â†’ S3 + CloudFront + ACM + Route 53), two-pass upload recipe (1-year immutable for hashed assets, no-cache for `index.html`), CORS-coupling note. `main.tf` is a `# TODO Sprint 25+` stub.
